چونکہ ہر ایک کا الگ الگ ثمن بیان کیا گیا ہے اس لئے اس کا ثمن بھی معلوم ہوگا۔ اور جب مبیع اور ثمن دونوں معلوم ہیں تو جواز بیع میں کیا شبہ ہوسکتا ہے۔ وقبول العقد في الذي فيه الخيار الخ سے ایک شبہ کا جواب ہے۔ شبہ یہ ہے کہ جس غلام میں خیار ہے وہ غلام حاکماً بیع میں داخل نہیں ہے یعنی وہ غیر مبیع ہے۔ اور دوسرا غلام جس میں خیار نہیں ہے وہ مبیع ہے تو گویا مبیع کے اندر بیع صحیح ہونے کے لئے غیر مبیع کے اندر بیع قبول کرنے کو شرط قرار دیا گیا اور یہ شرط مفسد بیع ہے۔ جیسا کہ غلام اور آزاد دونوں کو عقد واحد کے تحت فروخت کرنا مفسد بیع ہے کیونکہ غلام تو مبیع ہو سکتا ہے مگر آزاد مبیع نہیں ہو سکتا۔ جس طرح یہاں مبیع کے اندر بیع قبول کرنے کے لئے غیر مبیع کے اندر قبول کرنے کی شرط کی وجہ سے بیع فاسد ہو جاتی ہے اسی طرح منتقن کی دوسری صورت میں بھی بیع فاسد ہونی چاہئے تھی کیونکہ اس میں بھی وہی شرط ہے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ جس غلام میں خیار ہے وہ بیع کا محل ہے اور جب بیع کا محل ہے تو عقد بیع میں بھی داخل ہوگا اگرچہ ملکیت حاصل ہونے کے حق میں داخل نہیں ہوگا۔ پس جب وہ غلام جس میں مشتری کو تین دن کا خیار ہے محل بیع ہونے کی وجہ سے عقد میں داخل ہے تو بیع کے اندر بیع قبول کرنے کے لئے غیر مبیع میں قبول کرنے کی شرط لگانا لازم نہیں آتا ۔ اور جب یہ شرط لازم نہیں آتی تو بیع جائز ہوگی۔ اور مدبر کی مثال مطلق غلام کی ہے کہ مدبر میں بیع نافذ نہیں ہوتی مگر چونکہ مدبر مملوک ہونے کی وجہ سے محل بیع ہے اور محل بیع ہونے کی وجہ سے عقد بیع میں داخل ہے۔ اس لئے یہاں بھی مبیع یعنی غلام کے اندر بیع قبول کرنے کے لئے غیر مبیع کے اندر بیع قبول کرنے کی شرط لگانا لازم نہیں آیا اور چونکہ یہ شرط فاسد لگانا لازم نہیں آتا اس لئے غلام مطلق کی بیع جائز ہوگی۔ اس کے برخلاف اگر آزاد اور غلام کو ایک بیع میں جمع کیا تو بیع اس لئے فاسد ہوتی ہے کہ آزاد محل بیع قطعاً نہیں ہو سکتا نہ عقد بیع میں داخل ہوسکتا ہے اور نہ حکم بیع میں داخل ہو سکتا ہے۔ پس چونکہ آزاد قطعاً محل بیع نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے اس صورت میں مبیع یعنی غلام کے اندر بیع قبول کرنے کے لئے غیر مبیع یعنی آزاد کے اندر بیع قبول کرنے کی شرط لگانا لازم آتا ہے اور یہ شرط فاسد ہے اور شرط فاسد مفسد بیع ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے اس صورت میں بیع فاسد ہوگی۔ مسئلہ کی تیسری صورت یہ ہے کہ دونوں غلاموں میں سے ہر ایک کا ثمن تو علیحدہ علیحدہ بیان کر دیا گیا ہو مگر جس غلام میں خیار تھا اس کو معین نہیں کیا۔ چوتھی صورت یہ ہے کہ جس غلام میں خیار ہے اس کو تو متعین کر دیا گیا مگر ہر ایک کا ثمن علیحدہ علیحدہ بیان نہیں کیا گیا ان دونوں صورتوں میں عقد فاسد ہے تیسری صورت میں مبیع مجہول ہے کیونکہ جس غلام میں خیار ہے وہ حاکماً غیر مبیع ہے مگر معلوم نہیں کہ وہ کون سا غلام ہے پس جب یہ غیر معلوم ہے تو دوسرا غلام جو مبیع ہے وہ بھی غیر معلوم اور مجہول ہے اور مبیع کا مجہول ہونا مفسد بیع ہوتا ہے اس لئے اس صورت میں بیع فاسد ہو گی ۔ اور چوتھی صورت میں ثمن مجہول ہے کیونکہ دونوں کا ثمن علیحدہ علیحدہ بیان نہیں کیا گیا۔ پس معلوم نہیں کہ جس غلام میں خیار ہے اس کا ثمن کتنا ہے اور جس میں خیار نہیں ہے اس کا ثمن کتنا ہے ۔ حالانکہ مشتری پر فی الحال اسی غلام کا ثمن واجب ہے جس میں خیار نہیں ہے اور چونکہ ثمن مجہول ہونے کی وجہ سے بیع فاسد ہوتی ہے اس لئے اس صورت میں بھی بیع فاسد ہو جائے گی۔
Otherwise it is that: the one in which there is an option (khiyar) is determined, and the price (thaman) of each is not stated separately, and in both these cases the contract is void (fasid). Either because the subject of sale (mabi') is unknown or because the price is unknown. Explanation: The case is that a person sold two slaves for one thousand dirhams on the condition that the buyer has an option of three days in one of the two slaves, then the sale is void. And if he sold each of the two slaves for five hundred dirhams on the condition that the buyer has an option in a specific one of the two slaves, then the sale is valid. The author of al-Hidayah says that this issue has four forms. First: the price of neither slave is stated separately nor is the slave in which the buyer has the option specified; the first case of the matn is this. In this case the sale is void because both the subject and price are unknown. The subject is unknown because the slave in which the buyer has the option is excluded from the contract; that is, he is not in the price. Since in case of the buyer's option the buyer is not the owner of the subject, he has not become owner of the slave with the option; as if the contract did not take effect regarding the slave with the option. So only one of the two slaves enters the contract—the one without the option—and that slave is not known, so it is established that the subject is unknown. And since the price of each is not stated separately, the price is also unknown; and it has passed earlier that ignorance of either the subject or the price renders the sale void. So ignorance of both renders it void more certainly. The second form: the price of each slave is stated separately and the slave with the option is also specified; the second case of the matn is this. In this case the sale is valid because both subject and price are known. The subject is known because the slave with the option is specified, so the other slave is determined as the subject; and since the price of each is stated separately, the price is also known. And when both subject and price are known, what doubt can there be in the validity of the sale? And from 'and acceptance of the contract regarding that which has the option...' is a response to an objection. The objection is: the slave with the option is not legally included in the sale, i.e., he is non-subject, and the other slave without option is the subject; so to make the sale valid regarding the subject, acceptance of the sale regarding a non-subject is stipulated, and this stipulation invalidates the sale—just as selling a slave and a freeman together in one contract invalidates the sale because the slave can be a subject but the freeman cannot. Just as here the sale becomes void due to stipulating acceptance regarding non-subject for accepting the sale regarding the subject, similarly in the second form of the disagreement (the case of mudabbar) the sale should also be void. The answer is: the slave with the option is a locus (mahall) of the sale, and being a locus, he enters the contract though not regarding acquisition of ownership. So when the slave with the three-day option is included in the contract as a locus, it is not necessary to stipulate acceptance regarding a non-subject for accepting the sale regarding the subject. And when this stipulation is not necessary, the sale is valid. And the example of a mudabbar is like an absolute slave: sale of a mudabbar is not effective, but since he is owned, he is a locus of sale, and being a locus, he enters the contract. Therefore here too, it is not necessary to stipulate acceptance regarding a non-subject for accepting the sale regarding the subject (the slave). And since this invalid stipulation is not necessary, the sale of the absolute slave is valid. On the contrary, if a freeman and a slave are combined in one sale, the sale is void because the freeman cannot be a locus of sale at all, neither enters the contract nor its ruling. So there it is necessary to stipulate acceptance regarding a non-subject (the freeman) for accepting the sale regarding the subject (the slave), and this stipulation is invalid and invalidates the sale. Therefore the sale would be void. The third form: the price of each slave is stated separately but the slave with the option is not specified. The fourth form: the slave with the option is specified but the price of each is not stated separately. In both these cases the contract is void. In the third form the subject is unknown because the slave with the option is legally non-subject but it is not known which slave it is; when this is unknown, the other slave which is the subject is also unknown; and ignorance of the subject invalidates the sale. In the fourth form the price is unknown because the price of both is not stated separately; it is not known what the price of the slave with option is and what the price of the other is; whereas the buyer is currently obligated to pay the price for the slave without the option; and since ignorance of the price invalidates the sale, the sale is void.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from al-Hidayah, explaining the four forms of selling two slaves where the buyer has an option to choose one. The author first states the general rule: if the slave with the option is not specified or the price of each is not separate, the sale is void. Then he details four scenarios. In the first form (no specification, no separate price), both subject (mabi') and price (thaman) are unknown—the sale is void because the subject is unknown (the slave without option is indeterminate) and the price is unknown (since total price is not allocated). In the second form (both specified), the sale is valid because everything is known. Then an objection is raised: in the second form, the slave with option is not part of the sale, so accepting the contract for the subject requires a condition about a non-subject, which normally invalidates the sale (like slave+freeman). The response distinguishes: the slave with option is a locus (mahall) of the sale—he enters the contract though not for immediate transfer of ownership—so no condition of non-subject is needed. The mudabbar example reinforces this: he is a locus though sale is ineffective. The opposite case of slave+freeman is cited where the freeman is not a locus at all, so condition is needed and invalidates. Then the third and fourth forms are summarized: if only price is separate but option slave not specified, subject is unknown; if option slave specified but price not separate, price is unknown—both void. The commentary carefully follows al-Hidayah's reasoning, using analogy (qiyas) to distinguish cases based on whether the option-bearing item is a locus or not.

Key Terms
خیار (khiyar): Option; the right to rescind or confirm a sale within a specified period.
ثمن (thaman): Price; the consideration in a sale contract.
مبیع (mabi'): Subject matter of sale; the goods sold.
جہالت (jahala): Ignorance or uncertainty regarding an essential element (mabi' or thaman) that leads to invalidity.
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave whose master has declared that he will be free upon the master's death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the sale of two slaves with a condition that the buyer has a three-day option to choose one, which of the following makes the sale valid according to Hanafi fiqh?
A) The total price is set at 1000 dirhams, and the slave with option is unspecified.
B) Each slave is priced separately at 500 dirhams, and the slave with option is specified.
C) The price of each slave is not stated separately, but the slave with option is specified.
D) The price is stated for each separately, but the slave with option is not specified.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi sales law, a sale with a khiyar is valid if both the subject and price are known; jahala (ignorance) of either invalidates, except where istihsan allows tolerance.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Sale of Multiple Garments with Option to Choose
Ruling on multiple garment sale with option to choose

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a sale of multiple garments with khiyar al-ta'yin and explain the istihsan basis that distinguishes between three and four items.

Core Idea
A sale with option to choose is valid for up to three garments, but void for four—need limits the concession.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a specific transaction: buying multiple garments with the right to choose one within three days, at a fixed price. The Hanafi school, through istihsan, allows this for two or three garments but not for four. Understanding the rationale—how need (haja) and tolerable ignorance (jahala) justify the ruling—is key to grasping Hanafi legal method.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and the number limit
Read the passage to find that sale of two or three garments with option to choose is valid; for four it is void. Note the explicit ruling from al-Jami' al-Saghir.
The ruling is conditional on the option period (three days) and fixed price.
2
Understand the qiyas objection
The text states that by qiyas, the sale should be void in all cases due to jahala (ignorance) of the subject (which garment will be taken). This is the view of Zufar and al-Shafi'i.
Qiyas here is the default method; the Hanafi school departs from it via istihsan.
3
Analyze the istihsan rationale
Istihsan is based on two grounds: (1) the Shari'ah legislated khiyar to prevent loss (ghubn), allowing choice; (2) there is a real need for such transactions (e.g., buying for a third party). Both conditions must be present for the concession.
The need is considered met for up to three garments because three qualities (good, medium, poor) cover reasonable choices.
4
Note the threshold at three
The text explains that for three, ignorance does not lead to dispute because the chooser is known and the number is limited. For four, the need is not real, so the concession does not apply.
Thus, the ruling is not arbitrary but tied to a principled limit.
5
Contrast with opposing school
Zufar and al-Shafi'i follow strict qiyas: all such sales are void regardless of number. The Hanafi position is a rarity-based concession.
This illustrates how madhhab differences arise from different weights given to qiyas vs. istihsan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جس نے دو کپڑے اس شرط پر خریدے کہ ان میں سے جس کو چاہے دس درہم کے عوض لے لے اور یہ خیار تین دن تک ہے تو بیع جائز ہے اور تین اور چار کپڑوں پر اس طرح بیع فاسد ہے۔ قال و من اشترى ثوبين على ان ياخذ ايهما شاء بعشرة وهو بالخيار ثلاثة ايام فهو جائز وكذلك الثلثة فان كانت اربعة اثواب فالبيع فاسد والقياس ان يفسد البيع في الكل لجهالة المبيع وهو قول زفر و الشافعي وجه الاستحسان ان شرع الخيار للحاجة الى دفع الغبن ليختار ماهو الارفق والاوفق والحاجة الى هذا النوع من البيع متحققة لانه يحتاج الى اختيار من يثق به او اختيار من يشتريه لاجله ولا يمكنه البائع من الحمل اليه الا بالبيع فكان في معنى ماورد به الشرع غير ان هذه الحاجة تندفع بالثلث لوجود الجيد والوسط والردى فيها والجهالة لا تفضى الى المنازعة فى الثلث لتعيين من له الخيار وكذا في الاربع الا ان الحاجة اليها غير متحققة والرخصة ثبوتها بالحاجة وكون الجهالة غير مفضية الى المنازعة فلا تثبت باحدهما۔ ترجمہ جامع صغیر میں فرمایا کہ جس شخص نے دو کپڑے اس شرط پر خریدے کہ ان میں سے جس کو چاہے دس درہم کے عوض لے لے
Whoever bought two garments on condition that he take whichever of them he wishes for ten dirhams, and he has an option for three days, then the sale is valid. Similarly for three. But if there are four garments, the sale is void. He (Imam Muhammad) said: 'And whoever buys two garments on the condition that he take whichever of them he wishes for ten, and he has an option for three days, it is valid, and similarly for three. If there are four garments, the sale is void. The analogy (qiyas) is that the sale should be void in all due to ignorance of the subject (mabi'), and that is the view of Zufar and al-Shafi'i. The basis of istihsan is that the option (khiyar) is legislated due to need to avoid loss (ghubn), so that he may choose what is more suitable and fitting. And the need for this type of sale is real, because he may need to choose someone he trusts or choose for someone for whom he is buying, and the seller cannot bring them to him except through a sale. So it is in the meaning of what has been transmitted in the Shari'ah. However, this need is fulfilled by three garments because in them there are good, medium, and bad qualities, and ignorance does not lead to dispute in the case of three because the chooser is specified; similarly for four, except that the need is not real. And a concession (rukhsah) is established by need and the fact that ignorance does not lead to dispute; it is not established by either one alone.' Translation from al-Jami' al-Saghir: He said that the person who bought two garments on condition that he take whichever he wishes for ten dirhams...
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from al-Hidayah, citing al-Jami' al-Saghir. It addresses a sale of multiple garments where the buyer has an option to choose which one to take within three days, with a fixed total price (ten dirhams). The rule: for two garments it is valid; for three it is also valid; for four it is void. The author then reports the opposing view by qiyas: Zufar and al-Shafi'i consider all such sales void due to jahala of the subject (which garment will be taken). The Hanafi response is istihsan: the Shari'ah permits khiyar to prevent loss, and there is a genuine need for such transactions (e.g., buying for someone else, choosing a trusted product). This need is met by up to three garments because three qualities (good, medium, poor) cover reasonable choices; the ignorance does not lead to dispute because the option-holder is known and will choose later. For four, the need is not as pressing, so the concession does not extend. The commentary explains that both conditions—need and non-disputable ignorance—must be present for the concession; if either is missing, the general rule of jahala applies and the sale is void.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juridical preference; departing from qiyas for a stronger evidence of need or custom.
غبن (ghubn): Loss or disadvantage in a transaction; khiyar is meant to protect against it.
رخصت (rukhsah): Concession; a dispensation from the general rule due to need.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, buying four garments with the option to choose one within three days for a total price of ten dirhams is:
A) Valid by istihsan because the need exists.
B) Valid because jahala is the same as for two or three.
C) Void because jahala may lead to dispute and the need is not real.
D) Void only if the buyer is not reliable.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits a sale with option to choose up to three items due to need and tolerable ignorance, but prohibits four as need is not established.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate

Khiyar al-Ta'yin: Option to Choose Among Multiple Items
Ruling on khiyar al-ta'yin with istihsan justification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khiyar al-ta'yin and apply the distinction between qiyas and istihsan in sales with jahalah.

Core Idea
Khiyar al-ta'yin is valid for up to three items due to need—istihsan overrides qiyas.

In this passage from al-Hidayah, Al-Marghinani explains the Hanafi position on the option to choose among multiple items (khiyar al-ta'yin). While strict analogy (qiyas) would invalidate such a sale due to uncertainty of the sold item, the Hanafi school upholds its validity for two or three cloths based on juristic preference (istihsan) grounded in genuine need and the absence of likely dispute. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the limitation to three items.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is purchasing with khiyar al-ta'yin (option to choose). The ruling: valid for 2 or 3 cloths, invalid for 4 or more.
The matn explicitly states this.
2
Understand the qiyas objection
Qiyas would invalidate all such sales due to jahalah (ignorance of the sold item). This is the view of Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i.
Jahalah is a primary invalidator in sales.
3
Grasp the istihsan reasoning
Istihsan: the need for this type of sale is real (e.g., buyer chooses on behalf of another). It is similar to the need for khiyar al-shart, which is established in Shari'ah. Thus, the sale is allowed despite jahalah.
Need (hajah) and absence of dispute are the basis.
4
Note the limit: three items
The need is fulfilled with three cloths (good, medium, bad) and jahalah does not lead to dispute because the option holder will specify later. For four, the need is not pressing and jahalah may cause dispute.
The Hanafi position draws a line at three.
5
Recognize the ikhtilaf
Within Hanafi, Zufar disagrees; outside, al-Shafi'i agrees with qiyas. The mufta bihi is the Hanafi istihsan view.
Tarjih: need overrides strict analogy.

قال و من اشترى ثوبين على ان ياخذ ايهما شاء بعشرة وهو با لخيار ثلثة ايام فهو جائز وكذالك الثلثة فان كانت اربعة اثواب فالبيع فاسد والقياس ان يفسد البيع في الكل لجهالة المبيع وهو قول زفر و الشافعي وجه الاستحسان ان شرع الخيار للحاجة الى دفع الغبن ليختار ماهو الارفق والاوفق والحاجة الى هذا النوع من البيع متحققة لانه يحتاج الى اختيار من ثیق به او اختيار من يشتريه لا جله ولا يمكنه البائع من الحمل اليه الا بالبيع فكان في معنى ماورد به الشرع غير ان هذه الحاجة تندفع بالثلث لوجود الجيد والوسط والردى فيها والجهالة لا تفضى الى المنازعة فى الثلث لتعيين من له الخيار وكذافي الاربع الا ان الحاجة اليها غير متحققة والرخصة ثبوتها بالحاجة وكون الجهالة غير مفضية الى المنازعة فلا تثبت باحدهما.
ترجمہ جامع صغیر میں فرمایا کہ جس شخص نے دو کپڑے سے اس شرط پر خریدے کہ ان میں سے جس کو چاہے دس درہم کے عوض لے لے اور یہ خیار تین دن تک ہے تو یہ بیع جائز ہے اسی طرح تین کپڑوں (میں بھی جائز ہے ) پھر اگر چار کپڑے ہوں تو بیع فاسد ہے۔ اور قیاس یہ ہے کہ مبیع مجہول ہونے کی وجہ سے بیع تمام صورتوں میں فاسد ہو ۔ اور یہی امام زفر اور امام شافعی کا قول ہے۔ وجہ استحسان یہ ہے کہ خیار کی مشروعیت خسارہ دور ہونے کی ضرورت کے پیش نظر ہے تا کہ جو زیادہ نافع اور موافق ہو اس کو اختیار کرے۔ اور اس قسم کی بیچ کی حاجت بھی متفق ہے اس لئے کہ عقد کرنے والا اس شخص کے اختیار کرنے کی طرف محتاج ہو گا جس پر وہ اعتماد کرتا ہے یا اس شخص کے پسند کرنے کی طرف جس کے لئے خریدتا ہے اور بائع جمیع کو اس کے پاس لے جانے کی بغیر عقدی کے قدرت نہ دیگا۔ بس یہ بیچ بھی اس بیچ کے معنی میں ہو گئی ۔ جس پر شریعت وارد ہوئی ہے مگر یہ ضرورت تین کپڑوں سے دور ہو جاتی ہے۔ کیونکہ تین میں جید، ردی اور اوسط موجود ہیں۔ اور مین لہ الخیار کے متعین کرنے کی وجہ سے تین کپڑوں میں جہالت مفضی الی المنازعہ نہیں ہے۔ اور اسی طرح چار کپڑوں میں مگر اس کی طرف حاجت متحقق نہیں ہے حالانکہ اجازت کا ثبوت حاجت اور جہالت کے غیر مفضی الی المنازعہ ہونے کی وجہ سے ہوتا ہے، ہیں ان دونوں میں سے ایک بات سے اجازت ثابت نہ ہوگی۔
He said: And whoever buys two cloths on the condition that he takes whichever of them he wishes for ten dirhams, and he has the option for three days, it is permissible, and likewise for three. But if there are four cloths, the sale is invalid. And analogically, the sale would be invalid in all cases due to ignorance of the sold item, and that is the saying of Zufar and al-Shafi'i. The basis of istihsan is that the option is legislated due to the need to prevent loss, so that one may choose what is more suitable and agreeable. And the need for this type of sale is realized, because one needs to choose from someone he trusts, or choose for the sake of the one for whom he buys, and the seller cannot allow him to take them without a sale. So it is in the meaning of what came in the Shari'ah. However, this need is fulfilled with three, because good, medium, and bad are present in them, and ignorance does not lead to dispute in three because of the specification of the one who has the option. Similarly for four, but the need for it is not realized, and permission is established by need and by ignorance not leading to dispute, so it is not established by either one of them.
Translation of al-Jami' al-Saghir: He said: The person who bought two cloths on the condition that he takes whichever of them he wishes for ten dirhams, and this option is for three days, then this sale is permissible, and likewise for three cloths. Then if there are four cloths, the sale is invalid. And analogically, due to the sold item being unknown, the sale is invalid in all cases. And this is the saying of Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i. The basis of istihsan is that the legislation of the option is for the need to prevent loss, so that one may choose what is more beneficial and agreeable. And the need for this type of sale is also established, because the contracting party will be in need of the choice of the person he trusts, or the liking of the person for whom he buys, and the seller will not have the power to bring all to him without a contract. So this sale also became in the meaning of the sale upon which the Shari'ah came. However, this need is fulfilled by three cloths, because in three there are good, bad, and medium. And due to the specification of the one who has the option, ignorance does not lead to dispute in three cloths. And similarly in four cloths, but the need for it is not realized, whereas the establishment of permission is due to need and ignorance not leading to dispute. So permission will not be established by either one of these two.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the ruling on khiyar al-ta'yin (option to choose). The matn from al-Jami' al-Saghir states that buying two or three cloths with the condition that the buyer chooses which one to take within three days for a fixed price is valid, but for four cloths it is invalid. The commentator explains that analogically (qiyas), the sale should be invalid in all cases because the specific item sold is unknown, which is the view of Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i. However, the Hanafi school applies istihsan (juristic preference) based on need. The option (khiyar) is legislated to prevent loss, and here the need is genuine: the buyer may need to choose a cloth trusted by someone else or for the person he is buying for, and the seller will not allow carrying the cloths without a sale. This need for choosing among multiple items is similar to the need for khiyar al-shart (option of condition) which is established in Shari'ah. Therefore, by istihsan, khiyar al-ta'yin is allowed. However, this need is fulfilled with three cloths because they sufficiently cover quality variation (good, medium, bad). With four, the need is not as pressing, and the ignorance (jahalah) of the exact item could lead to dispute, so the sale becomes invalid. The principle is that permission (rukhas) is established only when both need and absence of dispute are present; if either is missing, the concession does not apply.

Key Terms
خیار تعیین (khiyār al-ta‘yīn): The option given to the buyer to choose which specific item among a set of items he will purchase, within a specified period (here, three days).
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas for a stronger reason, such as need or custom.
مبیع مجہول (mabī‘ majhūl): An unknown or unspecified sold item, which generally invalidates a sale due to gharar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the Hanafi school, buying with khiyar al-ta'yin (option to choose) is valid for how many cloths?
A) One or two cloths
B) Two or three cloths
C) Up to four cloths
D) Any number of cloths

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits khiyar al-ta'yin for up to three items based on istihsan, overriding the qiyas objection of jahalah.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
12 min
Khiyar al-Ta'yin: Balancing Necessity and Certainty in Sales
Inter-madhhab dispute on khiyar al-ta'yin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khiyar al-ta'yin and evaluate the qiyas vs istihsan argument underlying the dispute.

Core Idea
Hanafi school permits khiyar al-ta'yin up to three items based on necessity, but strict qiyas would reject it entirely.

This lesson examines the option of specification (khiyar al-ta'yin) in the Hanafi school, where a buyer purchases one unspecified item from a group. The ruling is not uniform; it depends on the number of items. The passage from Al-Hidayah presents the dispute between the Hanafi reliance on istihsan (juristic preference) and the opposing view based on qiyas. We will unpack the reasoning to understand why necessity limits the option to three cloths.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its limits
Identify the exact ruling: sale with khiyar al-ta'yin is valid for two or three cloths, but invalid (fasid) for four or more.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the opposing view and its proof
Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i hold the sale invalid in all cases. Their proof is qiyas: the sold object is unknown (majhul), which leads to dispute, so the sale is invalid.
Their asl is a sale with unknown object leads to dispute.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response using istihsan
The Hanafi response argues that necessity (hajah) justifies the sale, analogous to khiyar al-shart. When the buyer has the right to specify, ignorance becomes non-disputative (ghayr mufdi ila al-niza'). However, necessity is limited to three cloths because they cover good, bad, and average types.
Istihsan overrides qiyas in this case due to public need.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis allow such sales for up to three items; Shafi'is and Zufar consider them invalid regardless of the number.
This affects everyday transactions in Islamic markets.

تشریح عبارت میں ٹو بین سے مراد احد الثوبین ہے مجاز اگل بول کر جز مراد لیا گیا ہے۔ صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر ایک شخص نے دو یا تین کپڑوں میں سے ایک کپڑا دس درہم کے عوض اس شرط پر خریدا کہ وہ تین دن کے اندراندران کپڑوں میں سے ایک کپڑا متعین کرے گا تو یہ بیچ جائز ہے اور اگر چار کپڑوں میں سے ایک کپڑا اسی شرط کے ساتھ خریدا تو یہ بیچ فاسد ہے ۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ قیاس کا تقاضا تو یہ ہے کہ دو اور تین کپڑوں کی صورت میں بھی بیع فاسد ہو۔ کیونکہ مبیع فقط ایک کپڑا ہے اور وہ متعین نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے مجہول ہے اور مجہول بھی ایسا جو مفضی الی المنازعہ ہے کیونکہ کپڑے مالیت کے اعتبار سے متفاوت
ہوتے ہیں اور چونکہ مبیع کا مجہول ہونا مفید بیج ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے اس صورت میں بیچ فاسد ہے یہی قول امام زفر اور امام شافعی کا ہے۔ وجه استحسان یہ ہے کہ خیار شرط اس ضرورت سے مشروع ہوا ہے تا کہ من لہ الخیار تین دن میں غور و فکر کر کے خسارے اور دھو کے کو دور کرے اور جو اس کے لئے مناسب ہو اس کو اختیار کرے اور اسی طرح کی ضرورت خیار تعیین میں بھی موجود ہے کیونکہ بسا اوقات مشتری اس بات کا محتاج ہوتا ہے کہ جس پر اس کا بھروسہ ہے کپڑا وہ پسند کرے گا۔ اور کبھی اس کی پسند کا محتاج ہوتا ہے جس کے لئے خریدنا ہے۔ اور بائع بغیر عقد بیچ کے لے جانے کی اجازت نہیں دیتا تو وہ چند کپڑوں میں سے ایک کپڑا اخیار تعیین کی شرط کے ساتھ خریدنے کا محتاج ہوگا۔ پس خیار تعیین کی ضرورت خیار شرط کے معنی میں ہوگئی۔ اور خیار شرط کا جواز شریعت سے ثابت ہے تو خیا تعیین کو بھی خیار شرط کے ساتھ لاحق کر کے جائز قرار دیا جائے گا مگر چونکہ خیار تعیین کے جواز کا مدار ضرورت پر ہے اس لئے جہاں تک ضرورت ہے خیار سیمین وہیں تک جائز ہوگا۔ اور ضرورت تین کپڑوں سے پوری ہو جاتی ہے کیونکہ تین کپڑوں کے اندر تو خیار تعیین جائز ہوگا مگر چار کے اندر جائز نہ ہوگا۔ اور رہا تین کپڑوں کی صورت میں مبیع کا مجہول ہونا تو بلاشبہ مبیع مجہول ہے لیکن جب من لہ الخیار کو ایک کپڑا متعین کرنے کا اختیار دیدیا گیا تو یہ جہالت مفضی الی المنازعہ نہ ہوگی۔ اور جو جہالت مفضی الی المنازعہ نہ ہو وہ مفسد بیچ نہیں ہوتی ہے اس لئے اس صورت میں بیچ فاسد نہ ہوگی۔
رہا یہ سوال کہ چار کپڑوں میں بھی جب من لہ الخیار کو متعین کرنے کا اختیار دیدیا گیا تو جہالت مبیع مفضی الی المناز عد نہ رہی الہذا چار
کپڑوں کے اندر بھی خیار عین جائز ہونا چاہیئے تھا۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ خیار تعیین کا جائز ہونا دو باتوں پر موقوف ہے ایک تو یہ کہ حاجت جود دم یہ کہ جہالت غیر منقضی الی المنازعہ ہو۔ ان دونوں میں سے ایک سے جواز ثابت نہ ہوگا۔ اور چار کپڑوں میں مبیع کا مجہول ہونا حیات تعیین کی وجہ سے اگر چہ غیر مفضی الی المنازعہ ہے لیکن حاجت متحقق نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ تین کپڑوں میں جید ، ردی اور متوسط کے موجود ہونے کی وجہ سے تین کپڑوں سے ضرورت پوری ہو گئی ہے۔ اور چوتھا کپڑاز انداز ضرورت ہے۔ پس چار کپڑوں میں خیار تعیین کی ضرورت کی نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے خیار تعیین چار کپڑوں میں جائز نہ ہوگا۔
A commentary on Al-Hidayah, volume 8. And this khiyar is for three days, so this sale is valid. Similarly, in three cloths (it is valid). Then if there are four cloths, the sale is invalid. Qiyas is that due to the sold object being unknown, the sale is invalid in all cases. And this is the saying of Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i. The basis of istihsan is that the legislation of khiyar is due to the need to remove loss, so that one may choose what is more beneficial and suitable. And such need exists in this sale because the contracting party depends on the choice of the person he trusts or the person for whom he is buying, and the seller would not allow him to take them without a contract. So this sale becomes similar to the sale which the Shari'ah has legislated. But this need is fulfilled with three cloths, because in three there are good, bad, and average. And due to the right of specification, ignorance in three cloths does not lead to dispute. Similarly in four cloths, but need is not established, while permissibility is established due to need and ignorance not leading to dispute; without one of these two, permissibility is not established. Explanation: In the text, 'thawbayn' refers to 'one of the two cloths' figuratively. The case is: if a person buys one cloth from two or three for ten dirhams on condition that he will specify the cloth within three days, the sale is valid. If from four cloths under the same condition, the sale is invalid. The author of Al-Hidayah says: Qiyas requires that the sale be invalid even in the case of two or three cloths, because the sold object is only one cloth and it is unknown due to not being specified, and such ignorance leads to dispute because cloths differ in value. Therefore the sale is invalid. This is the view of Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i. The basis of istihsan is that khiyar al-shart is legislated due to the need for the one with the option to reflect and avoid loss and deception within three days, and to choose what is suitable. A similar need exists in khiyar al-ta'yin because sometimes the buyer needs the approval of a trusted person or the person for whom he is buying, and the seller does not allow taking the goods without a contract, so the buyer needs to buy one cloth from several with the condition of specification. Thus the need for khiyar al-ta'yin is similar to that of khiyar al-shart. Since khiyar al-shart is established by Shari'ah, khiyar al-ta'yin is also attached to it and declared valid. However, since the validity of khiyar al-ta'yin depends on necessity, it is valid only to the extent of necessity. Necessity is fulfilled with three cloths, so it is valid with three but not with four. As for ignorance in the case of three cloths, indeed the sold object is unknown, but when the one with the option is given the right to specify, this ignorance does not lead to dispute. Ignorance that does not lead to dispute does not invalidate the sale. Therefore the sale is not invalid in that case. As for the question: why should it not be valid in four cloths as well, since specification removes the dispute? The answer is that the validity of khiyar al-ta'yin depends on two things: need and ignorance that does not lead to dispute. With either one missing, permissibility is not established. In four cloths, although ignorance is removed by specification, need is not established because three cloths suffice with good, bad, and average. The fourth is beyond necessity. Therefore khiyar al-ta'yin is not valid in four cloths.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute explaining the Hanafi ruling on khiyar al-ta'yin (option of specification) in the sale of cloths. The ruling: if a buyer purchases one unspecified cloth from two or three cloths with the condition to specify within three days, the sale is valid according to the Hanafi school. If from four cloths, the sale is invalid. The passage presents the qiyas (analogical reasoning) that would make all such sales invalid due to the unknown nature of the sold object (majhul), which is the view of Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i. However, the Hanafi school adopts istihsan (juristic preference) based on necessity. The need for such a sale is analogous to khiyar al-shart (stipulated option), which the Shari'ah permits to prevent loss. This necessity is fulfilled with three cloths because they encompass the three categories (good, bad, average), so ignorance does not lead to dispute. For four cloths, necessity is not present. Thus the Hanafi position balances between allowing flexibility for genuine need and preventing excessive uncertainty that could lead to disputes.

Key Terms
خیار تعیین (khiyar al-ta'yin): The option of specification, where the buyer has the right to choose and specify one item from a group of items within a given period.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; departing from strict analogy (qiyas) for a stronger reason, often based on necessity, custom, or public interest.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning; extending a ruling from an original case to a new case due to a common effective cause ('illa).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Conditions of Khiyar al-Ta'yin: Requirement of Khiyar al-Shart and Duration
Intra-Hanafi dispute on conditions of khiyar al-ta'yin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the necessity of khiyar al-shart alongside khiyar al-ta'yin and explain the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the duration of khiyar al-ta'yin.

Core Idea
Khiyar al-ta'yin needs a defined period; Abu Hanifa says three days, the Sahibayn allow any known period.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses two interconnected issues: whether khiyar al-shart must accompany khiyar al-ta'yin, and what happens if it is not mentioned. The text reveals an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two distinguished students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn). Understanding the different narrations from Imam Muhammad's works helps clarify the underlying principles of khiyar (options) in sales.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two issues
First, note that the passage deals with (1) whether khiyar al-shart is required alongside khiyar al-ta'yin, and (2) the duration of khiyar al-ta'yin if khiyar al-shart is not mentioned.
These are distinct but related.
2
State the two narrations from Imam Muhammad's works
Al-Jami' al-Saghir includes a phrase indicating an option period (three days), suggesting khiyar al-shart is present. Al-Jami' al-Kabir omits this phrase, implying khiyar al-shart is not required. According to the latter, its mention is coincidental.
The source of the ikhtilaf is the different wording in these two primary texts.
3
Explain the positions on duration
When khiyar al-shart is not stipulated, Imam Abu Hanifa holds that khiyar al-ta'yin must be limited to three days, by analogy with khiyar al-shart. The Sahibayn allow any known period (e.g., one week, ten days), as long as it is definite.
This is the core intra-Hanafi dispute.
4
Analyze the reasoning
Abu Hanifa's view treats khiyar al-ta'yin as akin to khiyar al-shart, which is capped at three days by hadith. The Sahibayn see khiyar al-ta'yin as an independent option whose only condition is certainty of the period to avoid gharar.
The difference stems from how each views the nature of the option.
5
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
If a buyer takes two items with khiyar al-ta'yin and no khiyar al-shart, under Abu Hanifa he must decide within three days; under the Sahibayn, any pre-agreed period (e.g., one week) is valid. This affects contract drafting and enforcement.
The mufta bihi is the more flexible view of the Sahibayn.

Then it was said: It is required that in this contract there be khiyar al-shart along with khiyar al-ta'yin, and this is mentioned in Al-Jami' al-Saghir. And it was said: It is not required, and this is mentioned in Al-Jami' al-Kabir. So according to the latter, its mention is coincidental, not as a condition. And if khiyar al-shart is not mentioned, then according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) it is necessary to limit khiyar al-ta'yin to three days, while according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it may be any known period. Translation: Then it was said that in this contract, the presence of khiyar al-shart along with khiyar al-ta'yin is necessary, and this is mentioned in Al-Jami' al-Saghir. And it was said that it is not necessary, and this is mentioned in Al-Jami' al-Kabir. So according to Al-Jami' al-Kabir, the mention of khiyar al-shart is incidental, not as a condition. And when khiyar al-shart is not mentioned, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa it is necessary to time-limited khiyar al-ta'yin to three days, while according to the Sahibayn it may be any known period. Then in some copies, the wording 'he bought two cloths' is mentioned, and in some 'he bought one of the two cloths' is mentioned, and the latter is correct because in reality the sold object is one of them and the other cloth is a trust, and the first is a metaphor and borrowing. Explanation: The author of Al-Hidayah says that Imam Muhammad mentioned this issue in his two books, and there is a slight difference in their expressions. In Al-Jami' al-Saghir, the phrase 'and he has the option for three days' is mentioned, while in Al-Jami' al-Kabir, this phrase is not mentioned. According to the wording of Al-Jami' al-Saghir, the presence of khiyar al-shart is not necessary. And in Al-Jami' al-Saghir, the mention of khiyar al-shart is incidental, not as a condition. In any case, if khiyar al-shart is also mentioned along with khiyar al-ta'yin and the parties agree, then the buyer has the right to specify one cloth due to khiyar al-ta'yin and the right to cancel or confirm the sale due to khiyar al-shart. So if the buyer returns both cloths, it is valid due to khiyar al-shart; if he returns one cloth, it is by way of khiyar al-ta'yin. If khiyar al-shart is not mentioned along with khiyar al-ta'yin, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa the period of khiyar al-ta'yin is three days, and according to the Sahibayn it is any known period, whatever it may be. The author of Al-Hidayah says that in some copies of Al-Jami' al-Saghir, the wording 'he bought two cloths' is found, and in some 'he bought one of the two cloths' is found. The latter is more correct because the sold object is actually one cloth, and the other cloth is in the buyer's possession as a trust. The first wording is metaphorical and borrowed.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the conditions of khiyar al-ta'yin. It addresses two issues: (1) whether khiyar al-shart must be stipulated alongside khiyar al-ta'yin, and (2) the duration of khiyar al-ta'yin if khiyar al-shart is not mentioned. The text cites two different narrations from Imam Muhammad in his works: in Al-Jami' al-Saghir, the phrase 'and he has the option for three days' is included, implying that khiyar al-shart is present (since the option is mentioned). In Al-Jami' al-Kabir, no such phrase is mentioned, indicating that khiyar al-shart is not required. According to the latter, the mention of khiyar al-shart in the contract is coincidental, not a condition. If khiyar al-shart is not mentioned, then Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the khiyar al-ta'yin must be limited to three days, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) allow any known period. This difference stems from the nature of khiyar al-ta'yin: Abu Hanifa analogizes it to khiyar al-shart, which is limited to three days by hadith, while the Sahibayn see it as an independent option limited only by the need for a definite period. The passage also clarifies the correct wording of the contract: the buyer says 'I buy one of these two cloths' rather than 'I buy two cloths,' because the sale actually involves one cloth, with the other held as a trust (amana).

Key Terms
جامع صغیر (al-Jami' al-Saghir): One of the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, containing early Hanafi rulings.
جامع کبیر (al-Jami' al-Kabir): Another of the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah by Imam Muhammad, sometimes differing in wording from al-Jami' al-Saghir.
صاحبین (al-Sahibayn): The two companions of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, whose views often differ from Abu Hanifa.
خیار تعیین (khiyar al-ta'yin): The option to choose one item from a set within a specified period.
خیار شرط (khiyar al-shart): The option to cancel or confirm a sale within an agreed period, typically limited to three days.

C) One day by default.
D) The option is invalid without specifying a period.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires a defined period for khiyar al-ta'yin; the exact duration is disputed between Abu Hanifa (three days) and the Sahibayn (any known period).

Conditions for Valid Khiyar al-Ta'yin: The Three-Garment Limit
Explains the conditions limiting khiyar al-ta'yin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for the validity of khiyar al-ta'yin and explain why the Hanafi school limits it to three garments.

Core Idea
Khiyar al-ta'yin is valid only when there is genuine need and the uncertainty does not lead to dispute; beyond three garments, need is exceeded.

In this passage, we examine a specific limitation on the option of specification (khiyar al-ta'yin) in sales of garments. The Hanafi school permits this option only when two conditions are met: a legitimate need and uncertainty that does not lead to contention. The text explains why four garments exceed the need, making the contract irregular (fasid). Understanding this reasoning is essential for applying khiyar al-ta'yin correctly in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on khiyar al-ta'yin for garments
Recognize that the passage addresses whether the option of specification is permissible for garments at all, and then narrows it to a specific number. The default ruling: khiyar al-ta'yin is valid for up to three garments.
The ruling is derived from conditions of need and non-contentious ignorance.
2
Isolate the two conditions for validity
The passage states two prerequisites: (1) genuine need (hajah) for the option, and (2) the ignorance (jahalah) must be non-contentious (ghayr munqadi ila al-manaza'ah). Both must be present.
These conditions are from Hanafi usul al-fiqh: need permits certain relaxations, and uncertainty is tolerated if it does not lead to dispute.
3
Apply the conditions to the case of four garments
Examine why four garments fail the need condition: with three garments representing good, medium, and poor quality, the buyer's need is fully satisfied; a fourth is superfluous. Therefore, ignorance in four garments, though non-contentious, lacks the underlying need.
The same reasoning would apply to other commodities if three varieties suffice.
4
Conclude the operative legal ruling
The conclusion: khiyar al-ta'yin is invalid for four or more garments because the need condition is absent. The contract remains valid but the condition of option is void, making the contract fasid (irregular) according to Hanafi law.
If the contract is fasid, it may still be executable if the parties agree, but it does not have full legal effect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کپڑوں کے اندر بھی خیار عین جائز ہونا چاہیئے تھا۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ خیار تعیین کا جائز ہونا دو باتوں پر موقوف ہے ایک تو یہ کہ حاجت ہو اور دوسرے یہ کہ جہالت غیر منقضی الی المنازعہ ہو۔ ان دونوں میں سے ایک سے جواز ثابت نہ ہوگا۔ اور چار کپڑوں میں مبیع کا مجہول ہونا حیث تعیین کی وجہ سے اگر چہ غیر مفضی الی المنازعہ ہے لیکن حاجت متحقق نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ تین کپڑوں میں جید، ردی اور متوسط کے موجود ہونے کی وجہ سے تین کپڑوں سے ضرورت پوری ہو گئی ہے۔ اور چوتھا کپڑا زائد از ضرورت ہے۔ پس چار کپڑوں میں خیار تعیین کی ضرورت کے نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے خیار تعیین چار کپڑوں میں جائز نہ ہوگا۔
It should also be permissible to have khiyar al-'ain in the case of garments. The answer is that the permissibility of khiyar al-ta'yin depends on two things: one, that there is a need; and the other, that the ignorance is not contentious. With the absence of either, validity is not established. In the case of four garments, the uncertainty of the sold item due to specification, although not leading to contention, but the need is not realized because with three garments (good, bad, medium) the need is fulfilled, and the fourth garment is beyond need. Therefore, since there is no need for khiyar al-ta'yin in four garments, it is not permissible.

Commentary
This passage explains the legal reasoning behind limiting khiyar al-ta'yin to three garments. According to the Hanafi school, the option of specification (khiyar al-ta'yin) is permitted only when there is a genuine need and the uncertainty does not lead to dispute. In the case of four garments, the buyer's need is already satisfied by three (representing different qualities), so the fourth is superfluous, and thus the option is invalid. This ruling underscores the condition of need as a requirement for the validity of khiyar al-ta'yin.

Key Terms
خیار تعیین (khiyar al-ta'yin): The option for the buyer to choose and specify which item from a predefined set he wishes to purchase.
غیر منقضی الی المنازعہ (ghayr munqadi ila al-manaza'ah): Uncertainty that does not lead to dispute or contention between parties.
حاجت (hajah): Legitimate need that justifies relaxing normal contractual certainty.

Key Takeaway

The Option of Specification and Its Relationship with the Option of Stipulation
Ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute on khiyar al-ta'yin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on whether khiyar al-shart is required with khiyar al-ta'yin, and explain the timing rules for khiyar al-ta'yin according to Abu Hanifa and the two companions.

Core Idea
Khiyar al-shart is not required for khiyar al-ta'yin; if omitted, the buyer must specify within three days (Abu Hanifa) or any agreed period (Sahibayn).

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses an intra-Hanafi debate about the necessity of including a stipulation option (khiyar al-shart) when using the option of specification (khiyar al-ta'yin). It also clarifies the duration of the specification period when no stipulation is made. Understanding this ruling is essential for structuring valid contracts involving multiple goods.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two contested issues
First, determine that the passage discusses (a) whether khiyar al-shart is required alongside khiyar al-ta'yin, and (b) if not required, what is the timing for specification.
2
Note the two riwayat
Observe that al-Jami' al-Saghir states khiyar al-shart is required, while al-Jami' al-Kabir states it is not. This is the basis of the ikhtilaf.
The text mentions both books of Imam Muhammad.
3
Understand the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on timing
When khiyar al-shart is omitted, Abu Hanifa requires specification within three days; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allow any known period agreed by the parties.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school.
4
Recognize the textual nuance
The correct phrasing in the contract should be 'one of the two garments,' not 'two garments,' because only one item is the subject of sale; the other is held as a trust.
This affects the validity of the contract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم قيل يشترط ان يكون في هذا العقد خيار الشرط مع خيار التعيين وهو المذكور فى الجامع الصغير وقيل لا يشترط وهو المذكور فى الجامع الكبير فيكون ذكره على هذا الاعتبار وفاقا لا شرطا واذالم يذكر خيار الشرط لابد من توقيت خيار التعيين بالثلث عنده وبمدة معلومة ايتها كانت عندهما ثم ذكر في بعض النسخ اشترى ثوبين وفى بعضها اشترى احد الثوبين وهو الصحيح لأن المبيع فى الحقيقة احدهما والآخر امانة والاول تجوز واستعارة
Then it was said that it is necessary that in this contract there be the option of stipulation (khiyar al-shart) along with the option of specification (khiyar al-ta'yin), and this is mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir. And it was said that it is not necessary, and this is mentioned in al-Jami' al-Kabir. So its mention in the latter is by way of agreement, not as a condition. And when the option of stipulation is not mentioned, it is imperative to time the option of specification: according to him (Abu Hanifa) by three days, and according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) by a known period, whatever it may be. Then it is mentioned in some copies: 'he bought two garments' and in some copies: 'he bought one of the two garments' – and the latter is correct, because the actual sold item is one of them, and the other is a trust (amanah), and the first is a metaphor and borrowing.

Commentary
This passage addresses two issues: (1) the requirement of khiyar al-shart alongside khiyar al-ta'yin, and (2) the timing of khiyar al-ta'yin. According to al-Jami' al-Saghir, khiyar al-shart is required; according to al-Jami' al-Kabir, it is not, and its inclusion is merely advisory. If khiyar al-shart is omitted, then according to Abu Hanifa, the option of specification lasts three days; according to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it can be any agreed period. Additionally, the wording of the contract matters: the correct phrasing is 'one of the two garments,' not 'two garments,' because in reality only one is the subject of sale, the other being a trust.

Key Terms
خیار شرط (khiyar al-shart): The option of stipulation, allowing parties to cancel the contract within an agreed period.
جامع صغیر (al-Jami' al-Saghir): One of the six core books (Zahir al-Riwayah) of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.
جامع کبیر (al-Jami' al-Kabir): Another of the six core books by Imam Muhammad, sometimes differing slightly from al-Jami' al-Saghir.

D) The option becomes void immediately.

Key Takeaway
Khiyar al-shart is not a necessary condition for khiyar al-ta'yin; the specification period is three days (Abu Hanifa) or any agreed period (Sahibayn).

Rulings on Destruction or Defect in Khiyar al-Ta'yin
Rulings when one or both goods are destroyed or defective, and inheritance of options.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings when one or both of the two goods in a khiyar al-ta'yin contract are destroyed or become defective, and explain the reasoning based on the principles of lazim and amanah.

Core Idea
If one good is destroyed, its sale becomes binding; if both are destroyed, half the price of each is due.

Khiyar al-ta'yin allows the buyer to choose one of two specified goods after the contract. This lesson examines what happens when one or both goods are destroyed or become defective before the choice is made. The rulings hinge on whether the sale becomes binding or the goods remain a trust.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenarios
Recognize the two key scenarios: one good destroyed/defective, and both destroyed simultaneously. Note the different outcomes.
Both scenarios involve the buyer having possession of both goods as amanah.
2
Understand the ruling for one destroyed/defective
The sale becomes binding (lazim) on that specific good, and the other becomes a trust (amanah) because return due to defect is prevented.
The buyer must pay the price for the destroyed/defective good.
3
Understand the ruling for both destroyed
The buyer owes half the price of each good because the sale and trust are intermixed (shuyu') in both.
The intermixing prevents full liability on either.
4
Grasp the legal reasoning
The reason why one good becomes binding is the impossibility of returning a destroyed/defective item in khiyar al-ta'yin. For both destroyed, the proportionality arises from the commonality of sale and trust.
This reasoning is talil based on preventing return.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولوهلك احدهما او تعيب لزم البيع فيه بثمنه وتعين الآخر للامانة لامتناع الرد بالتعيب ولو هلكا جميعا معا يلزمه نصف ثمن كل واحد منهما للشيوع البيع والامانة فيهما ولو كان فيه خيار الشرط له ان يردهما جميعا ولو مات من له الخيار فلوارثه ان يرد احدهما لان الباقى خيار التعيين للاختلاط ولهذا لا يتوقت في حق الوارث فاما خيار الشرط لا يورث وقد ذكرناه من قبل
And if one of them is destroyed or becomes defective, the sale becomes binding on it with its price, and the other becomes determined as a trust (amanah), because return is prevented due to defect. And if both are destroyed simultaneously, half the price of each becomes due to him due to the commonality of sale and trust in them. And if there is khiyar al-shart (option of stipulation) in it, he has the right to return both. And if the one who has the option dies, his heir has the right to return one of them, because what remains is khiyar al-ta'yin due to mixing, and for this reason it is not timed in the right of the heir. As for khiyar al-shart, it is not inherited, and we have mentioned it before.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage covers four scenarios regarding khiyar al-ta'yin in a contract where the buyer has two garments with the option to specify one. First, if one garment is destroyed or becomes defective, the sale becomes binding for that specific garment, and the other becomes an amanah (trust) in the buyer's possession. Second, if both are destroyed simultaneously, the buyer owes half the price of each because the sale and trust are intermixed in both. Third, if there is also khiyar al-shart, the buyer can return both garments. Fourth, if the buyer dies, the heir inherits only khiyar al-ta'yin (not khiyar al-shart) and can return one garment; this right is not time-limited for the heir because the mixing prevents a definite period.

Key Terms
لزم البيع (lazima al-bay'): The sale becomes binding and irrevocable for that specific item.
امانت (amanah): A trust item in the buyer's possession, for which he is not liable unless negligent.
شیوع (shuyu'): Commonality or intermixing: the shared status of being partly sold and partly trust.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If both garments in a khiyar al-ta'yin contract are destroyed simultaneously, what must the buyer pay?
A) The full price of both garments.
B) Half the price of one garment.
C) Half the price of each garment.
D) Nothing, because both are trusts.

Key Takeaway
In khiyar al-ta'yin, destruction or defect of one good makes its sale binding; simultaneous destruction of both results in proportional liability due to intermixing.

Inheritance of Options in Khiyar al-Ta'yin
Rulings when one or both goods are destroyed or defective, and inheritance of options.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why khiyar al-ta'yin is inherited but khiyar al-shart is not, and state the heir's limited right to return one of the two goods without time limit.

Core Idea
The heir inherits only khiyar al-ta'yin, not khiyar al-shart, and can return one item without time limit.

This lesson continues with the fourth scenario: if the buyer dies, what options pass to the heir? The passage distinguishes between khiyar al-ta'yin, which is inherited, and khiyar al-shart, which is not. The reason given is that khiyar al-ta'yin involves mixing (ikhtilat) and thus is not time-bound for the heir.

Guided Path
1
Recall the previous scenarios
The passage earlier covered destruction/defect. Now it addresses the death of the option holder.
The same contract of khiyar al-ta'yin is assumed.
2
Identify the heir's right
The heir has the right to return one of the two goods (i.e., to exercise khiyar al-ta'yin).
This is limited to returning one, not both.
3
Understand why it is inherited
The remaining option is khiyar al-ta'yin due to mixing (ikhtilat), and it is not timed for the heir.
The mixing prevents a fixed period, so the heir can act at any time.
4
Distinguish from khiyar al-shart
Khiyar al-shart is not inherited; it expires upon the death of the option holder.
This is a critical difference: khiyar al-shart is a personal right tied to life.

And if one of them is destroyed or becomes defective, the sale becomes binding on it with its price, and the other becomes determined as a trust (amanah), because return is prevented due to defect. And if both are destroyed simultaneously, half the price of each becomes due to him due to the commonality of sale and trust in them. And if there is khiyar al-shart (option of stipulation) in it, he has the right to return both. And if the one who has the option dies, his heir has the right to return one of them, because what remains is khiyar al-ta'yin due to mixing, and for this reason it is not timed in the right of the heir. As for khiyar al-shart, it is not inherited, and we have mentioned it before.

Commentary
This passage covers four scenarios regarding khiyar al-ta'yin in a contract where the buyer has two garments with the option to specify one. First, if one garment is destroyed or becomes defective, the sale becomes binding for that specific garment, and the other becomes an amanah (trust) in the buyer's possession. Second, if both are destroyed simultaneously, the buyer owes half the price of each because the sale and trust are intermixed in both. Third, if there is also khiyar al-shart, the buyer can return both garments. Fourth, if the buyer dies, the heir inherits only khiyar al-ta'yin (not khiyar al-shart) and can return one garment; this right is not time-limited for the heir because the mixing prevents a definite period.

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): A stipulation option allowing either party to cancel the contract within a specified period.
اختلاط (ikhtilat): Mixing or intermixing of two goods, making it impossible to separate sale and trust.
لا يورث (la yurath): Not inherited; the right terminates with death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the heir inherit in a khiyar al-ta'yin contract?
A) The right to return both goods within a fixed time.
B) The right to return one good without time limit.
C) The right to cancel the entire sale.
D) Nothing; the option expires.

Key Takeaway
Khiyar al-ta'yin is inherited with a limited right to return one good, and without time limit, unlike khiyar al-shart which is not inherited.

Rulings on Garment Destruction in a Khiyar Ta'yin Sale
Ruling on destruction/defect in a khiyar ta'yin sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the legal consequences when one or both garments perish in a khiyar ta'yin sale, and explain why the heir's khiyar ta'yin is not time-limited.

Core Idea
Destruction/defect binds the sale for that garment; the other is amanah; upon death, khiyar shart ends but heir gets a fresh kiyar ta'yin.

This lesson examines a classical Hanafi scenario from the Hidayah: a buyer purchases two garments with an option to choose which one to keep (khiyar ta'yin), and possibly also a stipulation to rescind (khiyar shart). The passage details what happens when one or both garments are destroyed or become defective, and how the buyer's death affects these options. Understanding these nuanced rulings is essential for applying the principles of khiyar and amanah in sale contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract structure
Recognise that the sale involves two garments with khiyar ta'yin (the buyer must specify one within a time limit) and optionally also khiyar shart (a stipulated option to cancel the sale).
The default position is that the buyer has possession of both as a trust until he exercises his choice.
2
Determine the effect of destruction or defect of one garment
If one garment perishes or becomes defective, the sale becomes binding for that garment at its price, and the other garment becomes a pure amanah (trust) in the buyer's possession.
Return of the defective/destroyed garment is impossible, so it is as if the buyer chose it.
3
Determine liability if both garments perish together
If both are destroyed simultaneously, half the price of each garment is due because sale and amanah are spread equally over both.
The buyer is not liable for the full price because only half of each was subject to sale (the other half is amanah).
4
Analyse the effect of khiyar shart
If there is also khiyar shart, the buyer has the right to return both garments: one as an amanah and the other under the stipulated option.
This right exists as long as the khiyar shart period (usually three days) has not expired.
5
Examine the buyer's death and the heir's rights
Upon the buyer's death, the khiyar shart is not inherited and becomes void. However, the heir gains a new right of khiyar ta'yin to specify one garment, without any time limit, due to the mixing of ownerships.
This is not inheritance of the original option; it is a new right created to resolve the undivided ownership.

Source Text

اشتری ثوبین مجاز اور استعارہ ہے۔ یعنی گل بول کر جز مراد لیا گیا ہے۔
كتاب البيوع
ایک چیز ہلاک ہوگئی یا عیب دار ہو گئی اس کے شمن کے ساتھ بیچ درست ہے اور دوسری امانت ہوگی

ولوهلك احدهما او تعيب لزم البيع فيه بثمنه وتعين الآخر للامانة لا متناع الرد بالتعيب ولو هلكا جميعا معا يلزمه نصف ثمن كل واحد منهما الشيوع البيع والامانة فيهما ولو كان فيه خيار الشرط له ان يردهما جميعا ولو مات من له الخيار فلو ارثه ان يرد احدهما لان الباقى خيار التعيين للاختلاط ولهذا لا يتوقت في حق الوارث فاما خيار الشرط لا يورث وقد ذكرناه من قبل

ترجمہ اور اگر دونوں کپڑوں میں سے ایک تلف ہو گیا یا عیب دار ہو گیا تو اس میں اسکے شمن کے عوض بیچ لازم ہو جائے گی ۔ اور دوسرا کپڑا امانت ہونے کے لئے متعین ہو گیا کیونکہ عیب دار ہو جانے کی وجہ سے واپس کرنا ممتنع ہو گیا ہے۔ اور اگر دونوں ایک ساتھ ہلاک ہو گئے تو اس پر ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کا نصف ثمن لا زم ہوگا کیونکہ بیج اور امانت ان دونوں میں پھیلے ہوئے ہیں۔ اور اگر بیچ میں ( خیار تعیین کے ساتھ ) خیار شرط بھی ہو تو مشتری کے لئے ان دونوں کو واپس کرنے کا اختیار ہو گا۔ اور اگر وہ شخص مر گیا جس کے لئے خیار ہے تو اس کے وارث کو اختیار ہے کہ وہ ان دونوں میں سے ایک کو واپس کر دے۔ کیونکہ ملک مخلوط ہونے کیوجہ سے صرف خیار تعیین باقی ہے اور اسی وجہ سے وارث کے حق میں کوئی وقت متعین نہیں ہے۔ اور رہا خیار شرط تو اس میں میراث جاری نہیں ہوتی ہے اور ہم نے اس پہلے ذکر کر دیا ہے۔

تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ مشتری کے دونوں کپڑوں پر قبضہ کرنے کے بعد اگر ایک کپڑا ہلاک ہو گیا یا عیب دار ہو گیا تو اس کپڑے میں بیج لازم ہوگئی اور مشتری پر اس کا شمن واجب ہوگا۔ اور دوسرا کپڑ مشتری کے پہلے ہلاک شدہ کپڑے میں بیج اس لئے لازم ہوگی کہ ہلاکت یا عیب کی وجہ سے اس کپڑے کا واپس کرنا ممتنع ہو گیا ہے۔ پس جس کپڑے کا واپس کرنا ممتنع ہو گیا گویا مشتری نے اس کو اختیار کر لیا ہے اور جس کو مشتری اختیار کرلے اس میں بیج لازم ہو جاتی ہے اس لئے اس کپڑے میں بیج لازم ہوگی اور مشتری پر ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کا آدھا من واجب ہوگا کیونکہ عدم اولویت کی وجہ سے دونوں میں سے ہر ایک مبیع ہے اور ہر ایک امانت ہے یعنی بیع اور امانت دونوں میں شائع ہیں۔ پس چونکہ ہر ایک کپڑے کا نصف مبیع اور نصف امانت ہے یعنی بیج اور امانت دونوں میں شائع ہیں۔ پس چونکہ ہر ایک کپڑے کا نصف صبیح اور نصف امانت ہے اس لئے ہر ایک کپڑے کا نصف صبیح ہونے کی وجہ سے نصف ثمن واجب ہوگا اور نصف امانت ہونے کی وجہ سے اس کا تاوان واجب نہ ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ خیار تعیین کے ساتھ خیار شرط بھی ہوتو مشتری ان دونوں کپڑوں کو واپس کرنے کا اختیار رکھتا ہے اس لئے کہ مشتری ایک کپڑے میں تو امین ہے۔ لہذا اس کو بحکم امانت واپس کر سکتا ہے۔ اور دوسرے کپڑے میں مشتری ہے لیکن اس کے واسطے خیار شرط ہے تو اس کو خیار شرط کی وجہ سے واپس کر سکتا ہے اور اگر مشتری تین دن کے اندر اندر مر گیا تو اس کا خیار شرط باطل ہو گیا اور خیار تعیین باقی ہے۔ پس وارث کے لئے خیار تعیین کے تحت ایک کپڑا واپس کرنے کا اختیار ہو گا۔ خیار شرط تو اس لئے باطل ہو گیا کہ خیار شرط میں میراث جاری نہیں ہوتی ۔ جیسا کہ سابق میں بیان ہو چکا۔ اور رہا خیا تعیین تو وہ بطور میراث کے وارث کی طرف منتقل نہیں ہوا بلکہ مورث (میت) کا خیار تعیین تو موت کی وجہ سے باطل ہو گیا۔ مگر چونکہ دو کپڑوں میں سے ایک کپڑے کو متعین کئے بغیر مشتر کی مرگیا اور اس کپڑے کا مالک اس کا وارث ہو گیا تو وارث کی ملک بائع کی ملک کے ساتھ مل گئی اس لئے وارث کو ابتداء خیار تعیین کا حق دیا گیا تا کہ وہ اپنی ملک متعین کرے۔ وارث چونکہ میراث کے طور پر خار تعیین نہیں ہوتا۔ اسی لئے وارث کے حق میں خیار تحسین کی کوئی مدت متعین نہیں ہے حالانکہ مورث کے حق میں خیار تعیین کی مدینہ ہے۔ خواہ تین دن ہو جیسا کہ ابوحنیفہ گانا سب ہے۔ خواہ مدت معلومہ ہب ہو جیسا کہ صاحبین کا مذہب ہے۔ پس اگر وارث کے یہ رین میراث کے طور پر ثابت ہوتا تو وارث کے لئے بھی مدت متعین ہونی چاہئے تھی جیسا کہ مورث کے لئے متعین تھی ۔
He bought two garments (metaphorically, meaning part intended). Kitab al-Buyu'. If one of them perishes or becomes defective, the sale becomes binding in it at its price, and the other is determined for amanah, because returning due to defect is prevented. If both perish together, half the price of each is due on him due to the spread of sale and amanah in both. If there is also khiyar shart, he has the right to return both. If the one with the option dies, his heir has the right to return one of them, because the remaining is khiyar ta'yin due to mixing, hence no time limit is set for the heir. As for khiyar shart, it is not inherited, and we have mentioned it before. Translation: And if one of the two garments is destroyed or becomes defective, then the sale becomes binding in it at its price, and the other garment is determined to be amanah, because returning it is prevented due to defect. And if both perish together, half the price of each is due on him, because sale and amanah are spread in both. And if there is khiyar shart along with khiyar ta'yin, the buyer has the option to return both. And if the person with the option dies, his heir has the option to return one of them, because only khiyar ta'yin remains due to mixing, and hence no time is fixed for the heir. As for khiyar shart, it is not inherited, and we have mentioned it before. Commentary: The case is that after the buyer takes possession of both garments, if one garment perishes or becomes defective, the sale becomes binding in that garment and the buyer owes its price. The other garment remains as an amanah in the buyer's possession. Thus, if after the first garment perishes the second also perishes, no compensation is due from the buyer because of the principle 'amanat are not guaranteed.' The sale becomes binding in the first destroyed garment because returning it is prevented due to destruction or defect. Hence, returning is prevented, so it is as if the buyer has chosen it, and when he chooses it the sale becomes binding. Therefore the sale becomes binding in that garment, and half the price of each is due from the buyer because of lack of priority, each being both sold and amanah, i.e., sale and amanah are common in both. So each garment is half sold and half amanah, hence half price due for the sold half and no compensation for the amanah half. The author of Hidayah says: If there is khiyar shart along with khiyar ta'yin, the buyer has the right to return both garments, because in one garment he is an amin (trustee), so he can return it by virtue of amanah, and in the other garment he is the buyer but has khiyar shart, so he can return it by virtue of khiyar shart. And if the buyer dies within three days, his khiyar shart becomes void, but khiyar ta'yin remains. So the heir has the option, under khiyar ta'yin, to return one garment. Khiyar shart becomes void because it is not inherited, as previously mentioned. As for khiyar ta'yin, it is not transferred to the heir by inheritance; rather, the testator's khiyar ta'yin becomes void due to death. But because the buyer died without specifying one of the two garments, and his heir becomes owner of that garment, the heir's ownership mixes with the seller's ownership, so the heir is given the right of khiyar ta'yin anew so that he can specify his ownership. Since the heir does not inherit the khiyar ta'yin, there is no time limit set for the heir, whereas for the testator there is a time limit for khiyar ta'yin, whether three days as Abu Hanifa holds, or a known period as the Sahibayn hold. So if the heir's right were inherited, there would be a time limit for him as well, as there was for the testator.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling (hukm) from the Hidayah, expanded by the commentator. It addresses a sale with khiyar ta'yin (option of specification) of two garments. The ruling: If one garment perishes or becomes defective, the sale becomes binding for that garment at its price; the other becomes an amanah (trust) in the buyer's possession. If both perish at the same time, half the price of each is due, because sale and amanah are spread over both. If there is also khiyar shart (stipulated option), the buyer can return both garments. Upon death of the buyer, the khiyar shart is not inherited (it extinguishes), but the heir has a new right of khiyar ta'yin without time limit. The commentator clarifies that the khiyar ta'yin in the hands of the heir is not inherited from the deceased; rather, it arises anew due to the mixing of ownership. This explains why the heir's right is not time-bound, whereas the original buyer's khiyar ta'yin had a time limit (three days according to Abu Hanifa, or a known period according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). The passage also notes the principle 'amanat are not guaranteed' (al-amanat la tadman).

Key Terms
خیار تعیین (khiyar ta'yin): Option for the buyer to specify which of two items he wishes to purchase; if not specified within the period, the sale is confirmed for one by default.
خیار شرط (khiyar shart): Option stipulated by the buyer or seller to rescind the contract within a fixed period (usually three days).
امانت (amanah): Trust; in this context, the second garment is held in trust and is not guaranteed against loss without negligence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a buyer purchases two garments with khiyar ta'yin and both are destroyed simultaneously, what does the buyer owe?
A) The full price of both garments.
B) Nothing, because the sale is not yet confirmed.
C) Half the price of each garment.
D) The price of the cheaper garment.

Key Takeaway
In a khiyar ta'yin sale, destruction or defect triggers binding sale for that item; the other remains an amanah; upon buyer's death, the heir gets a fresh khiyar ta'yin without time limit.

Shuf'ah During Khiyar: Implied Consent
Ruling: buyer exercising shuf'ah during khiyar period shows acceptance of sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that a buyer's exercise of shuf'ah during khiyar shart cancels the option and confirms ownership from the time of purchase.

Core Idea
Exercising shuf'ah during khiyar implies permanent ownership, which voids the option.

This lesson examines a nuanced fiqh scenario: a buyer purchases a house with a three-day option, then during that option period acquires an adjacent house via shuf'ah. The Hanafi ruling is that this act constitutes consent to the original purchase, extinguishing the option. We will explore the logical proof based on the purpose of shuf'ah and the nature of ownership under khiyar shart, noting that this reasoning is specific to Imam Abu Hanifa's view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case
State the factual scenario: buyer buys house with khiyar shart; during khiyar another adjacent house is sold; buyer takes it by shuf'ah.
The option period is typically three days.
2
Identify the ruling
According to Abu Hanifa, the shuf'ah claim cancels the option and confirms ownership from the time of purchase.
This is the Hanafi position from Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Analyze the proof (talil)
Shuf'ah exists to remove harm from adjacency, which requires permanent ownership. Claiming shuf'ah implies the buyer considers himself permanent owner, so the option must have fallen.
The proof is based on qiyas reasoning linking purpose to implication.
4
Note specificity to Abu Hanifa
This reasoning is only needed for Abu Hanifa's madhhab because he holds that ownership transfers during khiyar (though conditional). For others, the ruling would differ.
Other schools may deny ownership transfer during khiyar.
5
Assess practical consequence
The option is cancelled; ownership is retroactive; shuf'ah is valid. If the option were still active, shuf'ah would be inconsistent.
This illustrates thamarah al-khilaf.

Source Text

And whoever buys a house on the condition that he has an option, then another house adjacent to it is sold, and he takes it by shuf'ah, then this is consent. Because seeking shuf'ah indicates his choice of ownership in the purchased house, since shuf'ah is only established to remove the harm of adjacency, and that is achieved by permanent ownership. So this implies that the option falls before the shuf'ah, thus ownership is established from the time of purchase, and it becomes clear that adjacency was established. This exposition is needed specifically for the madhhab of Abu Hanifa. Because seeking shuf'ah indicates that the buyer chooses ownership of the purchased house, since shuf'ah is only established to remove the harm of adjacency, and that is achieved by seeking permanent ownership. So seeking shuf'ah implies that before the shuf'ah, the option fell. Therefore ownership is established from the time of purchase, and it becomes clear that adjacency was established. This exposition is needed specifically for the madhhab of Abu Hanifa. Commentary: The case is that a person bought a house with a three-day option. Then during the option period, another adjacent house was sold. The buyer claimed the right of shuf'ah and took that house. This claiming of shuf'ah is an expression of consent, so the buyer's option is cancelled. The proof is that the buyer's request for shuf'ah indicates that he wants to establish his ownership in the purchased house. Because shuf'ah is established to remove the harm of adjacency, and adjacency is confirmed by permanent ownership in the purchased house. Permanent ownership demands ownership, and ownership is not established along with an option. So the option falls, and ownership is established from the time of purchase, and it becomes clear that at the time of the sale of the other house, adjacency existed. Because according to the Great Imam, the option enters into the buyer's ownership, so there is no problem for the buyer to claim shuf'ah for the other house.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage is a ruling (hukm) with proof, from the Hidayah. It addresses the case where a buyer purchases a house with a khiyar shart (option to rescind within a fixed period, here three days). During the option period, an adjacent house is sold to a third party, and the buyer exercises his right of shuf'ah (pre-emption) to acquire that adjacent house. The ruling: This act constitutes consent to the original purchase, thereby cancelling the option. The reasoning: Shuf'ah is a right that exists only to remove harm from an adjacent property (harm of a new neighbor). To have shuf'ah, one must be a permanent owner of the adjacent property. By claiming shuf'ah, the buyer demonstrates that he considers himself the permanent owner of the originally purchased house, which implies he accepts the sale and his option is extinguished retroactively from the time of the original purchase. This ruling is specifically according to Imam Abu Hanifa, because in his madhhab, when a sale is with an option, the buyer acquires ownership immediately (al-malk al-kamil remains weak), but once the option is waived, ownership is confirmed. Other imams may hold that ownership is not transferred during the option period. The commentator notes that this reasoning is necessary for Abu Hanifa's position.

Key Terms
شفعة (shuf'ah): Pre-emption right of a neighbor or partner to purchase a property sold to an outsider, to prevent harm from a new neighbor.
خیار شرط (khiyar shart): Stipulated option to rescind within a fixed period (e.g., three days) per the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because shuf'ah is a stronger right than khiyar.
B) Because shuf'ah requires permanent ownership, which is incompatible with an active option.
C) Because the seller's permission is implied.
D) Because the option period expires immediately.

Key Takeaway
Exercising shuf'ah during khiyar shart cancels the option because it implies acceptance of permanent ownership required for shuf'ah.
