اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد هشتم
واذا قبضه مستوراً سے ایک اعتراض کا جواب ہے۔
اعتراض یہ ہے کہ آپ کا یہ کہنا کہ مشتری کا وکیل، مشتری کے مانند ہے غلط ہے ہمیں یہ تسلیم نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ مشتری اگر میچ دیکھے بغیر مبیع پر قبضہ کرلے اور پھر مبیع دیکھ کر خیار کو بالقصد ساقط کر دے تو مشتری کا خیار رویت ساقط ہو جاتا ہے۔ لیکن اگر مشتری کے وکیل بالقبض نے بغیر دیکھے مبیع پر قبضہ کیا پھر مبیع کو دیکھ کر قصد اخیار رویت ساقط کیا تو اس سے مشتری کا خیار رویت ساقط نہیں ہوتا۔ پس ثابت ہوا کہ وکیل بالقبض مؤکل کے مانند نہیں ہے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ وکیل بالقبض نے مبیع پر بغیر دیکھے قبضہ کیا تو قبضہ کرتے ہی اس کی وکالت ختم ہو گئی اور جب وکیل کی وکالت ختم ہو گئی تو وہ مشتری کے حق میں اجنبی کے مانند ہو گیا اور کوئی اجنبی آدمی مشتری کے خیار رویت کے ساقط کرنے کا اختیار نہیں رکھتا۔ اسلئے وکیل کے مبیع پر بغیر دیکھے قبضہ کرنے کے بعد وکیل کو مشتری کا خیار رویت قصد اساقط کرنے کا اختیار نہ ہوگا۔ صاحبین کے قیاس کا جواب بخلاف خیار العیب سے صاحبین کے قیاس کا جواب ہے۔ جواب یہ ہے کہ خیار رویت کو خیار عیب پر قیاس کرنا درست نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ خیار عیب صفقہ کامل ہونے سے مانع نہیں ہے یعنی خیار عیب کے ہوتے ہوئے صفقہ نام اور کامل ہو جاتا ہے۔ جب صفقہ تام ہو جاتا ہے تو خیار عیب کے باوجود قبضہ بھی تام ہو جائے گا۔ اور خیار رویت کے ہوتے ہوئے صفقہ تام نہیں ہوتا۔ جیسا کہ پہلے گزر چکا۔ پس اس فرق کے ساتھ خیار رویت کو خیار عیب پر قیاس کرنا کس طرح درست ہوگا اور رہا خیار شرط تو وہ خود مختلف فیہ ہے۔ یعنی اگر کسی نے خیار شرط کے ساتھ کوئی چیز خریدی پھر مشتری نے کسی کو مبیع پر قبضہ کا وکیل بنا دیا اب اگر وکیل بالقبض نے مبیع کو دیکھ کر قبضہ کیا تو حضرت امام صاحب کے نزدیک مشتری کا خیار شرط ساقط ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک ساقط نہیں ہوتا۔ پس جب خیار رویت کی طرح خیار شرط بھی مختلف فیہ ہے اور امام صاحب کے نزدیک وکیل بالقبض کے مبیع کو دیکھ کر قبضہ کرنے سے مشتری کا خیار شرط بھی خیار رویت کی طرح ساقط ہو جاتا ہے تو صاحبین کا اپنے قول کو ثابت کرنے کیلئے خیار رویت کو خیار شرط پر قیاس کرنا کس طرح درست ہو گا۔
اور اگر یہ تسلیم کر لیا جائے کہ وکیل بالقبض کے مبیع کو دیکھ کر قبضہ کرنے سے بالا تفاق مشتری کا خیار شرط ساقت نہیں ہوتا ۔ اور یہی صحیح بھی ہے۔ تو اس کا جواب یہ ہوگا کہ وکیل بالقبض ، مؤکل یعنی مشتری کا قائم مقام ہوتا ہے اور خیار شرط کی صورت میں مؤکل اگر مبیع پر دیکھ کر قبضہ کرے تو خود موکل کا خیار شرط ساقط نہیں ہوتا۔ پس اسی طرح جو اس کا قائم مقام ہے یعنی وکیل اسکے قبضہ کرنے سے بھی مؤکل (مشتری) کا خیار شرط ساقط نہیں ہوگا ۔ اور رہا یہ کہ مشتری کے مبیع پر قبضہ کرنے سے اس کا خیار شرط ساقط کیوں نہیں ہوتا ۔ تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ خیار شرط کا مقصود بیع کے اچھا برا ہونے کو آزمانا ہے۔ اور یہ مقصد قبضہ کے بعد ہی پورا ہو سکتا ہے۔ اب اگر مبیع پر قبضہ کرنے سے مشتری کا خیار شرط ساقط ہو جائے تو خیار شرط کے مشروع ہونے کا مقصد ہی فوت ہو جائے گا۔ اسلئے کہا گیا کہ قبضہ بیع سے خیار شرط ساقط نہ ہوگا۔ حاصل یہ کہ جب موکل یعنی مشتری کے مبیع پر قبضہ کرنے سے اس کا خیار شرط ساقط نہیں ہوتا تو اس کے وکیل کے قبضہ کرنے سے بدرجہ اولی اس کا خیار شرط ساقط نہیں ہو گا۔
قاصد اور وکیل میں فرق اور رہا قاصد تو وہ وکیل کے مانند نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ قاصد نہ قبضہ نام کا اختیار رکھتا ہےاور نہ قبضہ ناقص کا بلکہ قاصد کا کام فقط پیغام پہنچا دینا ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر کوئی شخص بیچ کے سلسلہ میں قاصد ہو تو وہ نہ ثمن پر قبضہ کا مجاز ہے اور نہ جمیع سپرد کرنے کا مجاز ہے اور رہا وکیل تو اس کے سپر دتصرف ہوتا ہے تا کہ وہ اپنی رائے سے عمل کرے۔ چونکہ وکیل اور رسول ( قاصد ) دونوں الگ الگ دو حیثیتوں کے حامل ہیں اسی لئے رسول سے وکیل کا سلب کیا گیا ہے۔ چنانچہ ارشاد ہے قل لستُ عليكم بو کیل یعنی آپ فرمادیجئے کہ میں تم پر وکیل نہیں ہوں ۔ حالانکہ آپ کا رسول ہیں۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ وکیل اور رسول کا مفہوم جدا جدا ہے۔ اسلئے وکیل کو رسول پر قیاس کرنا بھی درست نہ ہوگا۔
Book of Sales. This is a response to an objection from 'and when he takes possession of it unseen...' The objection is that your statement 'the buyer's agent is like the buyer' is wrong; we do not accept it. Because if the buyer takes possession of the commodity without seeing it, and then sees it and intentionally drops the option, his option of sight is dropped. But if the buyer's agent for taking possession takes possession without seeing, then sees and intentionally drops the option of sight, the buyer's option of sight is not dropped. So it is proven that the agent for possession is not like the principal. The answer is that when the agent for possession took possession without seeing, his agency ended immediately upon possession, and when his agency ended, he became like a stranger to the buyer, and no stranger has the authority to drop the buyer's option of sight. Therefore, after the agent takes possession without seeing, he does not have the authority to intentionally drop the buyer's option of sight. The response to the analogy of the two companions (Sahibayn) is by contrasting with the option of defect. The answer is that it is not correct to analogize the option of sight to the option of defect, because the option of defect does not prevent the contract from being perfect; that is, despite the option of defect, the contract becomes complete and perfect. When the contract is complete, possession also becomes complete despite the option of defect. But with the option of sight, the contract is not perfect. As has passed before. So with this difference, how can analogizing the option of sight to the option of defect be correct? As for the option of stipulation, it is itself a matter of disagreement. That is, if someone buys something with an option of stipulation, then the buyer appoints someone as agent to take possession, now if the agent takes possession after seeing, according to Imam Abu Hanifa the buyer's option of stipulation is dropped, while according to the two companions it is not dropped. So when the option of stipulation is also disputed like the option of sight, and according to Imam Abu Hanifa the buyer's option of stipulation is also dropped by the agent's sighted possession, then how can the two companions' analogy of the option of sight to the option of stipulation to prove their own statement be correct? And if it is conceded that by the agent's sighted possession, the buyer's option of stipulation is not dropped by consensus, and this is indeed correct, then the answer is that the agent for possession is the representative of the principal, i.e., the buyer, and in the case of option of stipulation, if the principal takes possession after seeing, his own option of stipulation is not dropped. Similarly, the one who is his representative, i.e., the agent, his possession also will not drop the principal's (buyer's) option of stipulation. As for why the buyer's option of stipulation is not dropped by his own possession, the answer is that the purpose of the option of stipulation is to test whether the sale is good or bad, and this purpose can only be fulfilled after possession. Now if the buyer's option of stipulation were dropped by possession, the very purpose for which the option of stipulation was legislated would be lost. Therefore, it is said that possession does not drop the option of stipulation. The conclusion is that when the principal's (buyer's) own possession does not drop his option of stipulation, then a fortiori his agent's possession will not drop his option of stipulation. The difference between a messenger (qasid) and an agent (wakil): As for the messenger, he is not like the agent, because the messenger has authority neither for complete possession nor for incomplete possession; rather, the messenger's job is only to deliver the message. This is why, if someone is a messenger in a sale transaction, he is not authorized to take possession of the price nor to hand over the commodity. As for the agent, he is entrusted with the authority to act according to his own opinion. Since the agent and the messenger (rasul) have two distinct capacities, the agent is negated from the messenger. Thus the verse says: 'Say: I am not a guardian (wakil) over you' while he is a messenger. So it is known that the meanings of agent and messenger are separate. Therefore, analogizing the agent to the messenger is also not correct.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute and commentary on the Hidayah regarding the effect of the agent's (wakil bi al-qabd) actions on the buyer's khiyar al-ru'yah (option of sight). The commentator first presents an objection: the agent's dropping of the option does not affect the buyer because the agent's agency terminates upon taking possession, making him a stranger. This is a refutation of the claim that the agent is like the buyer. Then the commentator responds to Sahibayn's (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) analogy of khiyar al-ru'yah with khiyar al-'ayb (option of defect), explaining that the latter does not prevent the contract from being complete (tamam), unlike the former. This distinction invalidates the analogy. The discussion then shifts to khiyar al-shart (option of stipulation), where Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the agent's sighted possession drops the buyer's option, while Sahibayn disagree. The commentator argues that even if one accepts Sahibayn's view (that it does not drop), the agent's possession still should not drop it because the buyer's own possession does not drop his option of stipulation, as the purpose of testing requires post-possession evaluation. Finally, the commentator distinguishes between a wakil (agent) and a qasid (messenger): a messenger merely relays communication and has no authority over possession, while an agent has discretion. Hence, analogizing the agent to a messenger is invalid, supported by the Quranic verse (Qul lastu 'alaykum bi wakil) where the Prophet is a messenger but not a wakil. This passage is an expansion probe (sharh) on the Hidayah's text, clarifying nuanced differences between various options and the roles of representatives.

Key Terms
وکیل بالقبض (wakil bi al-qabd): An agent appointed specifically to take possession of the purchased commodity.
خیار رویت (khiyar al-ru'yah): The buyer's option to confirm or rescind a sale of an unseen item after seeing it.
خیار شرط (khiyar al-shart): An option stipulated by the buyer or seller to cancel the sale within a specified period.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why does the wakil bi al-qabd's dropping of khiyar al-ru'yah after taking possession without sight not affect the buyer?
A) Because the wakil is not authorized to drop options
B) Because the wakil's agency ends upon taking possession, making him a stranger
C) Because the buyer must drop the option himself personally
D) Because the wakil can only drop the option if he is also the buyer

Key Takeaway
The wakil bi al-qabd's sighted possession does not drop the buyer's khiyar al-shart because the wakil's agency ends upon possession, and the buyer's own possession does not drop it either.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Khiyar al-Ru'yah for a Blind Buyer
Ruling with proof on khiyar al-ru'yah for a blind buyer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state how a blind person's khiyar al-ru'yah falls under the Hanafi school and distinguish between the views of Abu Yusuf and Hasan b. Ziyad.

Core Idea
A blind buyer's khiyar al-ru'yah drops by touch, smell, taste, or description—not sight.

In this passage from al-Hidayah, al-Marghinani addresses the khiyar al-ru'yah for a blind buyer. He first confirms its validity, then explains how the option falls for movable and immovable property. Two intra-Hanafi opinions offer alternative methods, with the view of Hasan b. Ziyad preferred as closer to Abu Hanifa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
The text first establishes that a blind person's sale and purchase are valid, and he retains khiyar al-ru'yah because he bought an unseen item—just like a sighted person.
This overrides the misconception that a blind person cannot have khiyar.
2
Understand the means for movables
For movable goods, the option drops when the blind person touches, smells, or tastes the item, provided he recognizes it through that sense.
Analogous to a sighted person seeing the item.
3
Recognize the exception for immovables
For real estate, the option does not drop until a detailed description is given, because description substitutes for sight—similar to salam contracts.
Physical contact alone is not sufficient for land or buildings.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf holds that if the blind person stands where a sighted person would see and declares satisfaction, the option falls—by the principle of tashbih in incapacity. Hasan b. Ziyad recommends appointing a sighted agent to take possession while seeing it.
The text analogizes to a mute moving lips for recitation and a bald person passing a razor for shaving.
5
Apply the preferred view
The text states Hasan's view (appointing a wakil) is more similar to Abu Hanifa's statement, making it the relied-upon position: the agent's sight counts as the principal's.
This reflects the mufta bihi.

نابینا کیلئے خیار رویت کا طریقہ
قال وبيع الاعمى وشراه جائزوله الخيار اذا اشترى لانه اشترى مالم يره وقد قررناه من قبل ثم يسقط خياره بجسه المبيع اذاكان يعرف بالجس وبشمه اذا كان يعرف بالشم وبذوقه اذا كان يعرف بالذوق كمافي البصير ولا يسقط خياره فى العقار حتى يوصف له لان الوصف يقام مقام الرؤية كمافي السلم وعن ابى يوسف انه اذا وقف فى مكان لو كان بصير الراه وقال قدرضيت سقط خياره لان التشبيه يقام مقام الحقيقة في موضع العجز کتحریک الشفتين يقام مقام القراة فى حق الاخرس فى الصلوة واجراء الموسى مقام الحلق فى حق من لا شعر له فى الحج وقال الحسن يوكل وكيلا يقبضه وهو يراه وهذا اشبه بقول أبي حنيفة. لان رؤية الوكيل رؤية الموكل على ما مرانفا
ترجمہ اور نا بینا کی خرید و فروخت جائز ہے اور جب وہ خریدے تو اس کو خیار حاصل ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس نے ایسی چیز خریدی ہے جس کو اس نے نہیں دیکھا اور ہم اس کو سابق میں بیان کر چکے پھر اندھے کا خیار رویت طبیع کو ٹول کر چھونے سے ساقط ہو جائے گا جبکہ وہ ٹول کر چھونے سے پہچانی جاتی ہو اور سونگھنے سے ساقط ہوگا جبکہ سونگھ کر پہچانی جاتی ہو اور چکھنے سے ساقط ہو گا جبکہ وہ چکھنے سے پہچانی جاتی ہو ، جیسا کہ بینا کے حق میں ہے اور غیر منقولہ جائداد خریدنے کی صورت میں اس کا خیار ساقط نہ ہو گا۔ یہاں تک کہ اس کے واسطے وصف بیان کیا جائے کیونکہ وصف دیکھنے کے قائم مقام ہو جاتا ہے۔ جیسے بیع سلم میں ہے اور ابو یوسف" سے مروی ہے کہ اگر اندھا ایسی جگہ کھڑا ہو کہ اگر آنکھوں والا ہوتا تو طبیع کو دیکھ لیتا اور اس نے کہا کہ میں راضی ہوا تو اس کا خیار رویت ساقط ہو گیا۔ کیونکہ مقام عجز میں تشبیہ بھی حقیقت کے قائم مقام ہوتی ہے۔ جیسے نماز میں گونگے کے حق میں ہونٹ ہلا نا قرآت کے قائم مقام ہو جاتا ہے اور حج میں اس شخص کے حق میں جس کے سر پر بال نہ ہوں استرہ پھیرنا سر منڈانے کے قائم مقام ہوتا ہے۔ اور جس نے کہا کہ وہ ایک شخص کو وکیل کرے جو د یکھنے کی حالت میں طبیع پر قبضہ کرے۔ اور یہ ابوحنیفہ کے قول کے زیادہ مشابہ ہے۔ کیونکہ وکیل کا دیکھنا، موکل کا دیکھنا ہے۔ جیسا کہ ابھی ابھی گذرا ۔ تشریح صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ احناف کے نزدیک نابینا کی خرید و فروخت جائز ہے اور نا بینا اگر مشتری ہو تو اس کیلئے خنیار رویت بھی ثابت ہے۔ کیونکہ اس نے ایسی چیز خریدی ہے جو اس نے نہیں دیکھی اور ہم پہلے ثابت کر چکے کہ بغیر دیکھے ہوئے کسی چیز کو خریدنا جائز ہے۔ اور اس کے واسطے خیار رویت ثابت ہوتا ہے اور نابینا آدمی اس بینا آدمی کے مانند ہے جو بن دیکھے خریدتا ہے۔ پس اس نابینا کا بغیر دیکھے ہوئے کسی چیز کو خریدنا اور اس کیلئے خیار رویت کا ثابت ہونا جائز ہے۔ جیسے بینا کے حق میں جائز ہے۔ حضرت امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ اگر کوئی شخص پہلے بینا تھا اور پھر نا بینا ہو گیا تو اس کی خرید و فروخت تو بلاشبہ جائز ہے۔ اور اگر کوئی مادر زاد نا بینا ہوتو اس کی خرید و
Method of khiyar al-ru'yah for the blind. He (the author of Hidayah) said: The sale and purchase of a blind person is valid, and he has the option (khiyar) when he buys, because he bought something he has not seen, and we have established this before. Then his option drops by his touching the commodity if he recognizes by touch, and by his smelling if he recognizes by smell, and by his tasting if he recognizes by taste, just as for a sighted person. And his option does not drop in real estate (immovable property) until it is described to him, because description takes the place of sight, as in salam (advance payment sale). And from Abu Yusuf it is narrated that if he stands in a place where, had he been sighted, he would have seen the commodity, and he says 'I am pleased,' his option drops, because similitude (tashbih) takes the place of reality (haqiqah) in a situation of incapacity, like moving the lips takes the place of recitation (qira'ah) for a mute person in prayer, and passing the razor takes the place of shaving for someone with no hair in Hajj. And al-Hasan said: He should appoint an agent (wakil) who takes possession of the commodity while seeing it. And this is more similar to the statement of Abu Hanifa, because the sight of the agent is the sight of the principal, as has just passed. Translation: And the sale and purchase of a blind person is valid, and when he buys, he has the option, because he bought something he has not seen, and we have explained this earlier. Then the blind person's khiyar al-ru'yah drops by touching the commodity if it is recognized by touch, by smelling if it is recognized by smell, and by tasting if it is recognized by taste, just as for a sighted person. In the case of buying immovable property, his option will not drop until it is described to him, because description takes the place of sight, as in salam sale. And it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that if the blind person stands in a place where, had he been sighted, he would have seen the commodity, and he says 'I am pleased,' his option drops, because similitude takes the place of reality in a situation of incapacity, like moving the lips takes the place of recitation for a mute person in prayer, and passing the razor takes the place of shaving for someone with no hair in Hajj. And al-Hasan said that he should appoint a wakil who takes possession of the commodity while seeing it, and this is more similar to the statement of Abu Hanifa, because the sight of the wakil is the sight of the principal, as has just passed. Explanation: The author of Hidayah says that according to the Hanafis, the sale and purchase of a blind person is valid, and if the blind person is the buyer, he has khiyar al-ru'yah. Because he bought something he has not seen, and we have previously established that buying an unseen thing is valid, and for him khiyar al-ru'yah is established. And the blind person is like a sighted person who buys without seeing. So it is valid for a blind person to buy an unseen thing and for him to have khiyar al-ru'yah, just as it is valid for a sighted person. Imam Shafi'i has said that if a person was previously sighted and then became blind, his sale and purchase is undoubtedly valid. And if a person is born blind, then his purchase... (incomplete)
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (and some intra-Hanafi differences) on the khiyar al-ru'yah for a blind buyer. The text (from the Hidayah) states that a blind person's sale and purchase are valid, and he has the option of sight because he bought an unseen object. The option for a blind person falls by physical means appropriate to him: touching (if he recognizes by touch), smelling, or tasting, analogous to a sighted person's sight. For immovable property (real estate), the option does not fall until the property is described to him, because description replaces sight, as in salam contracts. Abu Yusuf adds that if the blind person stands in a position where a sighted person would see the item and declares satisfaction, his option drops—by the principle that in cases of incapacity, analogy (tashbih) substitutes for actuality, similar to a mute person moving lips for recitation or a bald person passing a razor for shaving. Hasan b. Ziyad (al-Hasan) recommends appointing an agent who sees the commodity and takes possession, which is closer to Abu Hanifa's view because the agent's sight is the principal's sight. The commentator then explains that this is the Hanafi position, and notes that Imam Shafi'i distinguishes between a person who became blind (valid sale) and a congenital blind person, but the text cuts off before completing Shafi'i's view.

Key Terms
نابینا (naabinaa): A blind person, whether born blind or became blind later.
جس (jass): Touching or feeling with the hand to recognize the object.
تشبیہ (tashbih): Similitude or analogy; here, treating the blind person's position of resembling a sighted person as sufficient for dropping the option in cases of incapacity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How does a blind person's khiyar al-ru'yah fall for immovable property according to the Hanafi school?
A) By touching or smelling the property
B) By standing at the property and declaring satisfaction
C) By having the property described to him
D) It never falls because he cannot see

Key Takeaway
A blind buyer's khiyar al-ru'yah falls by sensory recognition or description, not by sight, with intra-Hanafi differences on alternative methods.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Ruling on the Blind Person's Sale and Option of Inspection
Ruling on blind person's sale and khiyar al-ru'ya

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the blind person's transaction, explain how khiyar al-ru'ya falls for the blind, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Blind persons can transact validly; their option of inspection falls by senses or description, based on custom and necessity.

This lesson examines a unique fiqh scenario: the capacity of a blind person to engage in sales and purchases. The Hanafi school affirms its validity, detailing how the option of inspection (khiyar al-ru'ya) operates through touch, smell, taste, or description for real estate. We will also explore the Shafi'i objection and the Hanafi response grounded in prevalent practice (ta'āmul al-nās) and the principle of istihsān.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the core ruling: the sale and purchase of a blind person is valid (jā’iz), and the blind buyer retains khiyar al-ru’ya because he bought an unseen item.
This applies to both congenitally blind and those who lost sight later.
2
Explore khiyar al-ru'ya mechanisms
Analyze how the option falls: for movables, by touch, smell, or taste if the item is recognizable by that sense; for real estate, only by a thorough description.
Description substitutes for sight, analogized to salam (forward sale).
3
Identify the Shafi'i objection
State the opposing view: Imam al-Shafi'i holds that a congenitally blind person cannot transact at all because he lacks knowledge of colours and attributes.
Shafi'i considers description futile for one who has never seen.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Examine the two Hanafi proofs: (1) prevalent practice (ta'āmul al-nās) without objection is a valid shar‘ī proof; (2) necessity – otherwise the blind would starve, which is contrary to Islamic principles.
This is an istihsān argument overriding qiyas.
5
Note intra-Hanafi ikhtilāf on khiyar
Compare the views of Abu Yusuf (khiyar falls by standing where a sighted person would see) and Hasan ibn Ziyād (agent's seeing suffices). Relate to Abu Hanifa's principle.
The muftā bihī is comprehensive: all mechanisms are valid.

اگر آنکھوں والا ہوتا تو مبیع کو دیکھتا۔ پس ایسی جگہ کھڑے ہو کر نا بینا نے اپنی رضامندی کا اظہار کیا تو اس کا خیار رویت ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ اگر چہ مبیع کے اوصاف ذکر نہ کئے گئے ہوں کیونکہ بجز کی صورت میں تشبیہ، حقیقت کے قائم مقام ہو جاتی ہے۔ جیسے نماز میں گونگے کے حق میں ہونٹ ہلا نا قرآت کے قائم مقام ہے۔ اور حج میں گنجے کے حق میں سر پر استرا پھیرنا حلق کے قائم مقام ہے۔ اسی طرح نابینا کا ایسی جگہ کھڑا ہونا جہاں سے بینا آدمی کو مبیع نظر آسکتی ہو اس کے دیکھنے کے قائم مقام ہے۔ حسن بن زیاد نے فرمایا ہے کہ نابینا کسی کو اس بات کا وکیل کر دے کہ وہ مبیع دیکھ کر قبضہ کرے۔ حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ کے قول کے زیادہ مشابہ ہے۔ کیونکہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک وکیل کا دیکھنا مؤکل کے دیکھنے کی مانند ہے۔ جیسا کہ سابق میں گذر چکا ہے اور موکل کے مبیع دیکھنے سے اس کا خیار رویت ساقط ہو جاتا ہے لہذا وکیل کے دیکھنے سے بھی مؤکل کا خیار رویت ساقط ہو جائے گا۔
The sale and purchase of the blind person is valid, and he has the option when he buys, because he bought something he did not see, and we have established that previously. Then his option falls by his touching the sold item if it is known by touch, and by his smelling it if it is known by smell, and by his tasting it if it is known by taste, as for the sighted person. And his option does not fall in real estate until it is described to him, because description takes the place of sight, as in salam (forward sale). And it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that if he stands in a place where, had he been sighted, he would have seen the item, and he says 'I am satisfied,' his option falls, because comparison takes the place of reality in a situation of inability, like moving the lips takes the place of recitation for the mute in prayer, and passing a razor takes the place of shaving for him who has no hair in Hajj. And Hasan said: He should appoint an agent who takes possession while seeing it, and this is more similar to Abu Hanifa's statement, because the agent's seeing is the principal's seeing, as has passed earlier.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage is from the commentary on Al-Hidayah discussing the blind person's sale and purchase. It opens with the ruling that a blind person's transactions are valid, and if he is the buyer, he retains khiyar al-ru'ya (option of inspection) because he has purchased something he has not seen. This is analogous to a sighted person buying unseen goods. The passage then details how the option falls: for movable goods, if the blind can recognize the item by touch, smell, or taste, then after physically examining it in those ways, the option falls. For immovable property (real estate), the option does not fall until the seller describes the property thoroughly, because description substitutes for sight, similar to salam (advance sale) where the described goods are accepted without seeing. Then the text presents the view of Imam Abu Yusuf: if the blind person stands in a spot where a sighted person would see the item and declares satisfaction, the option falls, because in cases of inability, analogy substitutes for reality—analogous to a mute person moving lips as recitation in prayer, or a bald person passing a razor over his head as shaving in Hajj. Then Hasan ibn Ziyad is quoted: the blind person should appoint an agent who sees the item and takes possession; this is closer to Abu Hanifa's opinion because the agent's seeing is considered the principal's seeing. The Urdu commentary expands: it clarifies the Hanafi position, then presents Imam al-Shafi'i's view that a congenitally blind person (born blind) cannot transact at all because he lacks knowledge of colors and attributes, so describing the item is futile. The Hanafi response is twofold: first, people customarily transact with the blind without objection, and such common practice (ta'mul nas) is a valid legal proof, akin to consensus (ijma). Second, if a congenitally blind person cannot buy or appoint an agent, he would starve, which is unacceptable. Therefore, the Hanafi school holds that the transaction is valid for all blind persons. The commentary then reiterates the mechanisms for the option falling: for movables, by touch, smell, or taste; for immovables, by description; and includes Abu Yusuf's view of standing in a seeing place; and finally, Hasan ibn Ziyad's view of appointing an agent, which aligns with Abu Hanifa's principle that agent's seeing equals principal's seeing.

Key Terms
خیار رویت (khiyār al-ru'ya): The option of inspection granted to a buyer who purchases an unseen item; allows him to confirm the sale upon seeing it or return it if not satisfied.
نابینا (nābīnā): A blind person; in this context it refers to both congenitally blind and those who lost sight later.
تعامل الناس (ta'āmul al-nās): The prevalent practice of people; used as a proof for permissibility when consistent and unopposed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how does the khiyar al-ru'ya of a blind person fall for real estate?
A) By the blind person smelling the property
B) By the blind person touching the property
C) By a thorough description of the property
D) By the seller's guarantee

Key Takeaway
A blind person's transaction is valid in Hanafi law, and his khiyar al-ru'ya falls by touch, smell, taste, or description, based on istihsan and custom, not strict analogy.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate

Validity of a Blind-Born Person's Sale
Inter-madhhab dispute on blind-born person's sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the validity of a blind-born person's sale and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using ta'amul and hardship.

Core Idea
A blind-born person's sale is valid because customary practice and necessity override the objection of ignorance.

This passage presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that a blind-born person cannot know the qualities of goods, so their sale is invalid due to ignorance. The Hanafi school responds with two powerful proofs: universal customary practice (ta'amul) and the avoidance of hardship (haraj). Understanding this dispute reveals how Hanafi usul prioritizes real-world practice over theoretical impossibility.

Guided Path
1
State the Shafi'i position
Identify the Shafi'i argument: a blind-born person cannot know colors and qualities, so the sale is invalid due to ignorance (jahl).
2
Identify the first Hanafi rebuttal – ta'amul
The Hanafi school cites the continuous customary practice of Muslims (ta'amul al-nas) without objection, which is a valid legal proof akin to ijma.
Ta'amul is considered a hujja shar'iyya in Hanafi law.
3
Identify the second Hanafi rebuttal – hardship
The Hanafi school argues that if a blind person cannot buy, they would starve, leading to unacceptable hardship (haraj), a principle the Shafi'i school also accepts.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Compare the practical outcomes: Hanafi: sale is valid with khiyar al-ru'yah. Shafi'i: sale is invalid entirely.
5
Apply the Hanafi ruling to a scenario
Consider a blind-born tailor buying cloth. According to Hanafi law, the sale is valid, but the tailor has the option to return the cloth upon touching it if it is unsatisfactory.

كتاب البيوع
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد هشتم فروخت بالکل جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کو نہ رنگوں کا علم ہے اور نہ صفات کا علم ہے۔ اسلئے اس کے سامنے بیچ کے اوصاف اور رنگ بیان کرنا بے سود ہوگا ۔ اور جب صبیح کے اوصاف اور رنگوں کا بیان ممنوع ہے۔ اسلئے مادر زاد نابینا کی خرید و فروخت ناجائز اور ممنوع ہے۔ لیکن ہماری طرف سے جواب یہ ہے کہ لوگ مادر زاد اور غیر مادر زاد دونوں طرح کے اندھوں کے ساتھ خرید وفروخت کا معاملہ کرتے ہیں اور اس پر کوئی نگیر بھی نہیں کرتا اور بغیر نکیر کے تعامل ناس حجت شرعیہ ہے جیسا کہ مسلمانوں کا کسی چیز پر اجماع کرنا حجت شرعیہ ہے۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ مطلقاً نابینا کے ساتھ خرید و فروخت کرنا جائز ہے۔ دوسرا جواب یہ ہے کہ مادر زاد نا بینا اگر خرید وفروخت کا مالک نہیں ہے تو وہ دوسرے کو خرید و فروخت کے وکیل کرنے کا بھی مالک نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ ضابطہ یہی ہے کہ جو شخص خود خریدنے کا اختیار نہ رکھتا ہو۔ اس کو اپنی طرف سے دوسرے کو وکیل کرنے کا اختیار بھی نہ ہوگا۔ اب اگر مادر زاد تا بینا کو کھانے کی چیزوں کی ضرورت پیش آئے ۔ اور بقول امام شافعی کے نہ اس کو خریدنے کی اجازت ہے اور نہ خریدنے کا وکیل بنانے کی اجازت ہے تو وہ غریب بھوک سے تڑپ تڑپ کر جان دے گا۔ اور اسکی قباحت معمولی عقل رکھنے والے پر بھی مخفی نہیں ہے۔ چہ جائیکہ امام شافعی جیسے فاضل پرمخفی ہو۔ اسلئے مادر زاد نا بینا کی خرید وفروخت بھی جائز قرار دی گئی ہے۔ رہی یہ بات کہ نابینا کا خیار رویت کب ساقط ہو گا تو اس کا حکم یہ ہے کہ مبیع اگر ایسی چیز ہو جس کو ہاتھ سے مول کر پہچانا جاسکتا ہے تو مبیع ٹول کر چھونے سے نابینا کا خیار رویت ساقط ہو جائے گا اور اگر مبیع کوسونگھ کر پہچانا جاسکتا ہے تو سونگھنے سے اس کا خیار رویت ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ اور اگر چکھ کر پہچانا جا سکتا تو چکھنے سے اس کا خیار رویت ساقط ہو جائے گا ۔ جیسا کہ ان چیزوں میں بینا کا بھی یہی حکم ہے نابینا کا غیر منقولہ جائداد خریدنا
اور اگر نابینا آدمی نے کوئی غیر منقولہ جائداد خریدی مثلاً درخت خرید یا مکان خرید یا زمین خریدی تو اس کا خیار رویت ساقط نہ ہو گا۔ تا وقتیکہ مبیع کا بھر پور طریقہ سے وصف بیان نہ کر دیا جائے کیونکہ وصف بیان کرنا رویت کے قائم مقام ہوتا ہے۔ جیسے بیع سلم میں مسلم فیہ اگر چہ معدوم ہوتی ہے لیکن بیان وصف، مسلم فیہ کے قائم مقام ہوتا ہے۔ پس جس طرح بیع سلم میں مسلم فیہ کے بیان اوصاف کو مسلم فیہ کے قائم مقام قرار دیا گیا ہے۔ اسی طرح نابینا کے حق میں مبیع کے بیان وصف کو رویت کے قائم مقام مان لیا گیا ہے اور رویت صبیح کے بعد بیع پر راضی ہو جانے سے چونکہ خیار رویت ساقط ہو جاتا ہے۔ اسلئے نابینا کے سامنے اگر مبیع کا وصف بیان کر دیا گیا اور وہ اس پر راضی ہو گیا تو اس کا خیار رویت ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ حضرت امام ابو یوسف کی روایت یہ ہے کہ جب نا بینا ایسی جگہ کھڑا ہوا کہ اگر آنکھوں والا ہوتا تو مبیع کود یکھتا۔ پس ایسی جگہ کھڑے ہو کر نا بینا نے اپنی رضامندی کا اظہار کیا تو اس کا خیار رویت ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ اگر چہ میچ کے اوصاف ذکر نہ کئے گئے ہوں کیونکہ بجز کی صورت میں تشبیہ، حقیقت کے قائم مقام ہو جاتی ہے۔ جیسے نماز میں گونگے کے حق میں ہونٹ ہلا نا قرآت کے قائم مقام ہے۔ اور حج میں گنجے کے حق میں سر پر استرا پھیرنا حلق کے قائم مقام ہے۔ اسی طرح نابینا کا ایسی جگہ کھڑا ہونا جہاں سے بینا آدمی کو مبیع نظر آسکتی ہو اس کے دیکھنے کے قائم مقام ہے۔ حسن بن زیاد نے فرمایا ہے کہ نابینا کسی کو اس بات کا وکیل کر دے کہ وہ میچ دیکھ کر قبضہ کرے۔ حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ کے قول کے زیادہ مشابہ ہے۔ کیونکہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک وکیل کا دیکھنا مؤکل کے دیکھنے کی مانند ہے۔ جیسا کہ سابق میں گذر چکا ہے اور موکل کے مبیع دیکھنے سے اس کا خیار رویت ساقط ہو جاتا ہے لہذا وکیل کے دیکھنے سے بھی مؤکل کا خیار رویت ساقط ہو جائے گا۔
Translation omitted for length. The passage discusses the Shafi'i view that a blind-born person's sale is invalid due to ignorance of colors and qualities, and the Hanafi response that customary practice (ta'amul) and necessity (hardship) make it valid. Then it details the khiyar al-ru'yah for a blind person: terminated by touch, smell, or taste for tangible goods; for immovable property, by description; also Abu Yusuf's view on standing where a sighted person could see, and Hasan ibn Ziyad's view on appointing a deputy.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on the validity of a blind-born person's sale. The Shafi'i school argues that since a blind person cannot see the merchandise, the sale is invalid due to ignorance (jahl). The Hanafi school counter-argues with two points: (1) Customary practice (ta'amul) among Muslims, which is a valid legal proof, shows that blind people engage in transactions without objection, akin to ijma. (2) If a blind person cannot buy, they would starve, leading to hardship—a principle the Shafi'i school also accepts. Therefore, Hanafis rule the sale valid. The passage then addresses the khiyar al-ru'yah (option of seeing) for a blind person: It is terminated for movable goods by alternative senses (touching, smelling, tasting) as with a sighted person. For immovables, since these cannot be fully sensed, khiyar remains until comprehensive description is given, analogous to salam contracts. Abu Yusuf adds that if the blind person stands where a sighted person could see and expresses satisfaction, khiyar is terminated by analogy to a mute person's lip movement in prayer. Hasan ibn Ziyad reports that the blind person may appoint a deputy to see and take possession, which aligns with Abu Hanifa's view that the deputy's sight suffices.

Key Terms
خیار رویت (khiyar al-ru'yah): The option for the buyer to return the purchased item upon seeing it if it does not meet satisfaction, for having purchased it sight unseen.
تعامل ناس (ta'amul al-nas): The customary practice of Muslims that is universally accepted without objection, used as a legal proof.
مادر زاد نابینا (madar zad nabina): A person born blind (blind from birth).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary Hanafi proof for validating a blind-born person's sale?
A) Explicit Quranic verse
B) Customary practice (ta'amul) without objection
C) Analogical reasoning (qiyas) with animals
D) Consensus of the Companions

Key Takeaway
Hanafi law validates a blind-born person's sale based on customary practice and necessity, granting the buyer khiyar al-ru'yah to protect against ignorance.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
7 min
Termination of Khiyar al-Ru'yah for a Blind Person
Ruling on termination of khiyar al-ru'yah for blind buyer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the methods by which a blind person's khiyar al-ru'yah is terminated, and distinguish the views of Abu Yusuf and Hasan ibn Ziyad.

Core Idea
A blind person's khiyar ends by alternative senses for movables, by description for immovables, or by standing in view of the object.

After establishing that a blind-born person's sale is valid, the text details how the option to return (khiyar al-ru'yah) is terminated for such a buyer. Unlike a sighted person who sees the item, a blind person uses other senses or receives detailed description. The passage also records important intra-Hanafi differences, particularly from Imam Abu Yusuf and Hasan ibn Ziyad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
Khiyar al-ru'yah is terminated when the buyer acquires sufficient knowledge of the purchased item and expresses satisfaction.
2
List methods for movable goods
For items that can be recognized by touch, smell, or taste, the blind person's khiyar is terminated by using those senses.
Same as for a sighted person.
3
List the method for immovable goods
For immovables (land, buildings), khiyar is not terminated until a comprehensive description is given and the blind person accepts.
Analogy to salam contract.
4
Note Abu Yusuf's alternative
Abu Yusuf holds that if the blind person stands where a sighted person could see the item and expresses satisfaction, khiyar is terminated, even without description.
Analogy to mute's lip movement in prayer and bald's razor stroke in hajj.
5
Note Hasan ibn Ziyad's view
Hasan ibn Ziyad reports that the blind person may appoint a deputy to see and take possession; the deputy's sight suffices to terminate khiyar.
This aligns with Abu Hanifa's principle that the deputy's sight equals the principal's sight.

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on the validity of a blind-born person's sale. The Shafi'i school argues that since a blind person cannot see the merchandise, the sale is invalid due to ignorance (jahl). The Hanafi school counter-argues with two points: (1) Customary practice (ta'amul) among Muslims, which is a valid legal proof, shows that blind people engage in transactions without objection, akin to ijma. (2) If a blind person cannot buy, they would starve, leading to hardship—a principle the Shafi'i school also accepts. Therefore, Hanafis rule the sale valid. The passage then addresses the khiyar al-ru'yah (option of seeing) for a blind person: It is terminated for movable goods by alternative senses (touching, smelling, tasting) as with a sighted person. For immovables, since these cannot be fully sensed, khiyar remains until comprehensive description is given, analogous to salam contracts. Abu Yusuf adds that if the blind person stands where a sighted person could see and expresses satisfaction, khiyar is terminated by analogy to a mute person's lip movement in prayer. Hasan ibn Ziyad reports that the blind person may appoint a deputy to see and take possession, which aligns with Abu Hanifa's view that the deputy's sight suffices.

Key Terms
خیار رویت (khiyar al-ru'yah): The option for the buyer to return the purchased item upon seeing it if it does not meet satisfaction.
بیع سلم (bay' al-salam): A forward sale where payment is made in advance for goods to be delivered later, described precisely.

Checkpoint
How is a blind person's khiyar al-ru'yah terminated for a house?
A) By touching the walls
B) By comprehensive description
C) By smelling the rooms
D) By tasting the doorknob

Key Takeaway
A blind person's khiyar al-ru'yah is terminated by alternative senses for movables and by description for immovables, with additional views from Abu Yusuf and Hasan ibn Ziyad.

Seeing One Garment, Buying Two: Must Return Both
Ruling on returning both garments when buyer saw only one before purchase

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for when a buyer sees only one of two purchased garments and explain the proofs from the prohibition of tafriq al-safqah and khiyar al-ru'yah.

Core Idea
If you buy two garments after seeing only one, you cannot return just the unseen one—you must return both or keep both.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a common scenario in khiyar al-ru'yah: a buyer purchases two garments after seeing only one. The ruling clarifies that the option of sight applies to the unseen item, but the buyer cannot return it alone without violating the prohibition of splitting the transaction (tafriq al-safqah). Understanding this ruling requires grasping two key principles: the non-uniformity of garments (so sight of one does not substitute for another) and the unity of the contract until all options are resolved.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
Read the matn: a person sees one of two garments, buys both, then sees the other. The ruling: he may return both garments (jā'iz lahu an yaruddahumā). Note that he cannot return only the unseen one.
The ruling is permissive (mubāḥ) as a right, not an obligation.
2
Understand the first proof: khiyar al-ru'yah applies to unseen
Because garments differ in value (tafāwut fī al-thiyāb), seeing one is not sufficient for the other. Hence khiyar al-ru'yah remains for the unseen garment. This is based on the earlier principle that heterogeneous items require individual sight.
Cf. homogeneous items like grain where seeing a sample may suffice.
3
Understand the second proof: prohibition of tafriq al-safqah
Returning only the unseen garment would split the transaction before completion (tafriq al-safqah qabl al-tamām). The Prophet ﷺ forbade this. Since khiyar al-ru'yah keeps the contract incomplete, partial rescission is invalid.
The hadith is referenced but not quoted verbatim in this passage.
4
Analyze the legal effect: faskh min al-aṣl
When the buyer returns both garments, the contract is rescinded from the origin (faskh min al-aṣl), as if never concluded. This is because full consent (riḍā) was not established without seeing all items.
This contrasts with a rescission from that point onward (iqālah).
5
Note the practical consequence and cross-madhhab difference
The Hanafi position: no partial return. The Shāfiʿī school may allow returning only the unseen item if the contract can be split. Understanding the thamarah al-khilāf (practical difference) is key.
The difference hinges on whether the transaction is viewed as a single unit or as multiple independent sales.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دو کپڑوں میں سے ایک کو دیکھا اور دونوں کو خرید لیا پھر دوسرے کو دیکھا تو ایک کی رویت دوسرے کی رویت کیلئے کافی نہیں
قال ومن راى احد الثوبين فاشتراهما ثم راى الاخر جاز له ان يردهما لان رؤية احدهما لاتكون رؤية الآخر للتفاوت في الثياب فبقى الخيار فيما لم يره ثم لا يرده وحده بل يردهما كيلا يكون تفريقا للصفقة قبل التمام وهذا لان الصفقة لاتتم مع خيار الرؤية قبل القبض وبعده ولهذا يتمكن من الرد بغير قضاء ولارضاء ويكون فسخا من الاصل

کا دیکھنا نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے جس کپڑے کو نہیں دیکھا اس میں خیار باقی رہے گا۔ پھر اسی کو تنہا واپس نہیں کرے گا بلکہ دونوں کو واپس کرے گا تا کہ صفقہ تمام ہونے سے پہلے تفریق نہ ہو اور اس لئے کہ قبضہ سے پہلے بھی اور قبضہ کے بعد بھی خیار رویت کے ساتھ صفقہ تمام نہیں ہوتا ہے اور اسی وجہ سے مشتری کو بغیر قضاء قاضی اور بغیر بائع کی خوشنودی کے مبیع واپس کر دینے کا اختیار ہے اور یہ عقد اصل سے مسخ شمار ہوتا ہے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے دو تھان میں سے ایک تھان دیکھ کر دونوں کر خرید لیا۔ پھر دوسرے تھان کو دیکھا تو مشتری کو خیار رویت کے تحت دونوں تھان واپس کر دینے کا اختیار ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ سابق میں گذر چکا کہ اشیاء متفاوت الآحاد میں سے ایک شی کا دیکھنا تمام کیلئے کافی نہیں ہوتا بلکہ ہر ایک کو علیحدہ علیحدہ دیکھنا ضروری ہے۔ پس اس اصول کی روشنی میں ایک تھان کے دیکھنے سے دوسرے تھان کا دیکھنا شمار نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ کپڑوں میں مالیت کے اعتبار سے بڑا تفاوت ہوتا ہے۔ اسلئے مشتری نے جس تھان کو نہیں دیکھا ہے اس میں خیار رویت حاصل ہوگا ۔ مگر خیار رویت کی وجہ سے فقط اسی ایک تھان کو واپس کرنے کا اختیار نہ ہو گا۔ بلکہ اگر واپس کرنا چاہتا ہے تو دونوں تھان واپس کرنا ضروری ہے۔ کیونکہ اگر مشتری نے ایک تھان واپس کیا اور جس کو خریدنے سے پہلے دیکھ لیا تھا اس کو واپس نہ کیا تو صفقہ تمام ہونے سے پہلے تفریق صفقہ لازم آئے گا۔ حالانکہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے تفریق صفقه قبل التمام سے منع فرمایا ہے۔ اسلئے ایک تھان واپس کرنا اور ایک واپس نہ کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور تفریق صفقه قبل التمام اس لئے لازم آتا ہے کہ خیار رؤیت کے ہوتے ہوئے صفقہ پورا نہیں ہوتا خواہ مشتری نے مبیع پر قبضہ کیا ہو یا قبضہ نہ کیا ہو چونکہ خیار رویت کے ساتھ صفقہ تمام نہیں ہوتا۔ اس لئے مشتری کو یہ اختیار ہے کہ وہ بغیر قضاء قاضی اور بغیر رضائے بائع کے عقد کو رد کر دے۔ اور یہ بیچ کو رد کرنا اصل ہی سے مسخ ہوگا۔ یعنی گو یا منعقد ہی نہیں ہوئی ہے۔ کیونکہ مبیع کے اوصاف معلوم نہ ہونے سے مشتری کی رضامندی متحقق نہیں ہوئی۔ اور مشتری کی رضا کے بغیر بیع منعقد نہیں ہوتی۔ اسلئے اس صورت میں گویا بیچ کا انعقاد نہیں ہوا۔
Heading: 'Seeing one of two garments and buying both, then seeing the other – the sight of one is not sufficient for the other.' Matn: 'He who saw one of two garments and bought both, then saw the other: he has the right to return both, because seeing one is not seeing the other due to differences in garments. So the option remains for what he did not see. Then he does not return it alone but returns both, so as not to split the transaction before completion. This is because the transaction is not completed with the option of sight, before or after possession. Therefore he is able to return without court order or consent, and it is a rescission from the origin.' Translation: 'And whoever sees one of two cloths and buys both, then sees the other: he has the option to return both cloths, because due to differences in cloths, seeing one is not seeing the other. So the option remains for the cloth he did not see. Then he will not return it alone but will return both, so that the transaction is not split before completion, and because before and after possession, the transaction is not complete with the option of sight. So the buyer has the right to return the goods without court order or seller's consent, and this is a rescission from the origin. Explanation: The scenario is that if someone saw one of two cloths and bought both, then saw the other, the buyer has the option of sight to return both cloths. The proof is that earlier it passed that for heterogeneous items, seeing one is not sufficient for all; each must be seen separately. So in light of this principle, seeing one cloth does not count as seeing the other, because cloths differ greatly in value. Therefore the buyer has khiyar al-ru'yah for the unseen cloth. However, due to khiyar al-ru'yah, he does not have the right to return only that one cloth; rather, if he wishes to return, he must return both. Because if he returns one cloth and does not return the one he saw before purchase, splitting the transaction before completion (tafriq al-safqah qabl al-tamam) would be necessary, whereas the Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited splitting the transaction before completion. So returning one and not the other is not permissible. And splitting the transaction before completion becomes necessary because with the option of sight, the transaction is not complete, whether the buyer has taken possession or not. Since the transaction is not complete with khiyar al-ru'yah, the buyer has the option to rescind the contract without court order and without the seller's consent. And this rescission of the sale is a dissolution from the origin, as if the contract was never concluded, because the buyer's consent was not actualized due to unknown attributes, and without the buyer's consent the sale is not concluded.'
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the matn of Al-Hidayah with commentary. The ruling: if a person sees one garment and then buys two garments (including the unseen one), upon later seeing the second garment, he has the option to return both—not just the unseen one. The proof is twofold. First, due to the inherent value differences in garments, seeing one is not a substitute for seeing the other (unlike homogeneous items like grain, where seeing a sample may suffice). Thus, khiyar al-ru'yah applies to the unseen garment. Second, the buyer cannot return only the unseen garment because that would split the transaction (tafriq al-safqah) before it is complete—a practice prohibited by the Prophet ﷺ. The transaction is incomplete as long as the khiyar al-ru'yah remains, even after possession. Therefore, the buyer must either keep both or return both. If he returns, it is a rescission (faskh) from the origin, meaning the contract is treated as void ab initio because the buyer's full consent was not established without seeing all items. This ruling highlights the Hanafi principle that khiyar al-ru'yah prevents finalization of the contract, and that multiple items sold in one transaction cannot be partially rescinded when some were unseen.

Key Terms
تفريق صفقة (tafriq al-safqah): Splitting a single transaction into parts before it is fully completed, such as returning only one item from a multi-item sale.
فسخ من الأصل (faskh min al-asl): Rescission of the contract from its origin, treating it as void ab initio.
صفقة (safqah): The transaction or deal, particularly the striking of a bargain in a single sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person buys two garments after seeing only one, and then sees the second, what must he do to return the unseen garment?
A) Return only the unseen garment
B) Return both garments
C) Keep both garments
D) Ask the seller's permission to return one

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a buyer cannot partially rescind a multi-item sale when some items were unseen; the contract must be fully rescinded or fully upheld.

Khiyar al-Ru'yah Void by Death
Ruling that khiyar al-ru'yah is nullified upon death of the holder

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that khiyar al-ru'yah is void upon the death of the holder and distinguish it from inheritable options.

Core Idea
Death of the holder extinguishes khiyar al-ru'yah; it is a personal right, not inheritable.

In Hanafi sales law, the option of sight (khiyar al-ru'yah) grants the buyer a window to rescind after inspecting the item. This lesson clarifies that this right is personal and lapses upon the buyer's death—unlike some other options. Understanding this distinction prevents heirs from wrongly asserting the right to reject a sale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the right and its nature
Khiyar al-ru'yah is a buyer's right to cancel a sale after seeing the item if dissatisfied. It is personal to the buyer.
2
State the triggering event
The event that extinguishes the option is the death of the holder (the buyer).
3
State the legal consequence
Upon death, the option becomes void (batil). The heirs do not inherit the right to inspect and rescind.
Contrast with khiyar al-shart which is inheritable.
4
Explain the rationale
The option is tied to the buyer's personal satisfaction; after death, that need ceases. Therefore, inheritance does not apply to it.
The text says: 'because inheritance does not run in it according to us.'
5
Distinguish from khiyar al-shart
Khiyar al-shart (option of stipulation) is a contractual right that can be inherited, as it is based on an agreement that can continue.
The author references previous discussion on khiyar al-shart.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خیار رویت موت سے باطل ہو جاتا ہے
ومن مات وله خيار الرؤية بـطـل خيـاره لانه لا يجرى فيه الارث عندنا وقد ذكرنا في خيار الشرط
The option of sight becomes void by death. And whoever dies and he has the option of sight, his option becomes void, because inheritance does not apply to it according to us, and we have mentioned it in the option of stipulation.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This is a concise ruling from the matn: khiyar al-ru'yah (the option of seeing) is an inalienable personal right that does not pass to the deceased's heirs. Unlike khiyar al-shart (option of stipulation), which may be inheritable, khiyar al-ru'yah is extinguished upon death. The reason is that khiyar al-ru'yah is based on the buyer's personal inspection and satisfaction; after death, the need for inspection ceases. Hanafi law treats it as non-heritable (lā yajrī fīhi al-irth) in contrast to some other options.

Key Terms
خیار رویت (khiyar al-ru'yah): The option of the buyer to rescind the contract upon seeing the purchased item if it does not please him.
موت (mawt): Death of the holder of the option.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, what happens to khiyar al-ru'yah when the buyer dies?
A) It passes to his heirs
B) It becomes void
C) It continues until sight by the heirs
D) It converts to khiyar al-shart

Key Takeaway
Khiyar al-ru'yah is void upon the death of the holder; it is a personal right not subject to inheritance.

Khiyar al-Ru'yah: Returning Both Garments When Only One Seen
Ruling on returning both garments after seeing the second

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that khiyar al-ru'yah requires returning all items in a single purchase when only one was seen, and explain the reasoning based on tafriq al-safqah.

Core Idea
If you buy two garments after seeing one, you must return both or keep both — no splitting.

When a buyer purchases multiple items after seeing only one, the Hanafi school applies the principle of khiyar al-ru'yah (option of sight) in a way that preserves the unity of the contract. This lesson examines a specific ruling from the Hidayah: if you see one of two garments and buy both, then see the other and dislike it, you cannot return only the unseen garment. Instead, you must return both. The reasoning is that returning only one would split the contract (tafriq al-safqah) before it is completed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act: buying two garments after seeing only one, then seeing the other. Ruling: the buyer may return both garments, but not just the unseen one.
This is a specific application of khiyar al-ru'yah.
2
Trace the legal reasoning (ta'lil)
Why must he return both? Because seeing one does not give knowledge of the other (due to variation among garments), so khiyar remains for the unseen. But returning only that would split the contract, which is prohibited.
The prohibition of tafriq al-safqah is based on hadith.
3
Understand the consequence of khiyar
As long as khiyar exists, the contract is not complete. Therefore, rescission does not require court or consent and voids the contract from the start.
This shows the strength of the option in Hanafi law.
4
Apply to similar scenarios
If someone buys multiple items after seeing only a sample, the same rule applies: all must be returned or none.
The key is the unity of the transaction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن راى احد الثوبين فاشتراهما ثم راى الاخر جاز له ان يردهما لان رؤية احدهما لاتكون رؤية الآخر للتفاوت في الثياب فبقى الخيار فيما لم يره ثم لا يرده وحده بل يردهما كيلا يكون تفريقا للصفقة قبل التمام وهذا لان الصفقة لاتتم مع خيار الرؤية قبل القبض وبعده ولهذا يتمكن من الرد بغير قضاء ولارضاء ويكون فسخا من الاصل
He said: Whoever sees one of two garments and buys both, then sees the other, it is permissible for him to return both. Because seeing one does not constitute seeing the other due to the variation among garments, so the option remains regarding what he has not seen. Then he does not return it alone but rather returns both, so that there is no splitting of the contract before its completion. And this is because the contract is not completed with the option of sight before or after possession, and therefore he is able to return without a court ruling or consent, and it is a rescission from the origin.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on khiyar al-ru'yah (option of sight) when multiple items are purchased after seeing only one. The Hanafi position is that the buyer has the right to return all items, not just the unseen one, to prevent tafriq al-safqah (splitting the contract) before completion. The reasoning is that since each garment may vary greatly in value, seeing one does not give knowledge of the other, so the khiyar remains for the unseen item. However, returning only that item would split the single transaction, which is prohibited by hadith. Thus, the buyer must return both or keep both. The contract remains incomplete as long as the khiyar exists, so the buyer can rescind without court order or seller's consent, and the rescission voids the contract ab initio.

Key Terms
خيار الرؤية (khiyar al-ru'yah): The buyer's option to rescind a contract upon seeing the merchandise if it does not meet his approval, based on lack of prior knowledge of its attributes.
الصفقة (al-safqah): The contract or transaction as a whole, including all items sold together.
تفريق الصفقة (tafriq al-safqah): Dividing the contract by returning part of the merchandise while keeping the rest, before the contract is finalized.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a buyer sees one of two garments and purchases both, then sees the second and dislikes it, what must he do to exercise his khiyar al-ru'yah?
A) Return only the unseen garment.
B) Return only the seen garment.
C) Return both garments.
D) Keep both and demand a price reduction.

Key Takeaway
When multiple items are bought after seeing only one, the option of sight applies to the entire contract; the buyer must return all items or keep all.
